Workers at some state-run plants put down their tools, left the buildings and chanted slogans outside. Hundreds of students also rallied on university campuses in Minsk while clapping, chanting and forming solidarity chains. At least 155 people were arrested for supporting the strike action in Minsk, Barysaw, Brest, Hrodno, Mogilev and Novopolotsk.<ref name="10-26" />

On 28 October, 4 Belarusian anarchist activists were arrested near the Belarusian-Ukrainian border.<ref name=nav0111>{{cite web|url=https://naviny.media/new/20201101/1604219951-zaderzhannyh-na-granice-anarhistov-podozrevayut-v-atakah-na-zdaniya|title=–ó–∞–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∞–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö –Ω–∞ –≥—Ä–∞–Ω–∏—Ü–µ –∞–Ω–∞—Ä—Ö–∏—Å—Ç–æ–≤ –ø–æ–¥–æ–∑—Ä–µ–≤–∞—é—Ç –≤ –∞—Ç–∞–∫–∞—Ö –Ω–∞ –∑–¥–∞–Ω–∏—è –≥–æ—Å–æ—Ä–≥–∞–Ω–æ–≤ –≤ –°–æ–ª–∏–≥–æ—Ä—Å–∫–µ –∏ –ú–æ–∑—ã—Ä–µ|language=ru|date=1 November 2020|access-date=23 November 2020|publisher=Naviny}}</ref> The government and state media accused them of terrorism.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://ont.by/news/anarhisty-gotovili-terakty-na-territorii-belarusi|title=–ê–Ω–∞—Ä—Ö–∏—Å—Ç—ã –≥–æ—Ç–æ–≤–∏–ª–∏ —Ç–µ—Ä–∞–∫—Ç—ã –Ω–∞ —Ç–µ—Ä—Ä–∏—Ç–æ—Ä–∏–∏ –ë–µ–ª–∞—Ä—É—Å–∏|language=ru|date=31 October 2020|access-date=23 November 2020|publisher=ONT}}</ref> They were charged under criminal code articles 289 (terrorism; up to the death penalty) and 295 (arms trafficking; up to 12 years in prison).<ref name=nav0111 />

On 31 October, hundreds of women marched in central Minsk, chanting "Freedom" and "Fair Elections" as they carried red-and-white flags and banners.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.rferl.org/a/nelarus-hundreds-women-march-against-lukashenka-threats/30922776.html|title=Hundreds Of Women March Against Lukashenka Despite Threats|work=Radio Free Europe|date=2020-10-31|access-date=2020-11-02|lang=en}}</ref> About 40 people were detained in Minsk, Hrodna, and other Belarusian cities.<ref name="11-01" />

===November===
On 1 November, about 20,000 demonstrators marched in Minsk. They gathered in eastern Minsk and headed toward [[Kurapaty]] where over 200,000 people were executed during the [[Great Purge]].<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.rferl.org/a/belarusian-security-forces-detain-protesters-/30924550.html|title=Belarusian Security Forces Detain Protesters|work=Radio Free Europe|date=2020-11-01|access-date=2020-11-12|lang=en}}</ref> Protesters carried banners with slogans such as "The people's memory (lasts) longer than a life of a dictatorship" and "Stop torturing your people!". Ahead of the march, security forces had already cordoned off several central squares in Minsk, closed several metro stations and mobile internet was disrupted.<ref name=dw_11-01>{{Cite news|url=https://www.dw.com/en/belarus-protesters-face-crackdown-as-protest-draws-tens-of-thousands/a-55467124|title=Belarus protesters face crackdown, as protest draws tens of thousands|work=Deutsche Welle|date=2020-11-01|access-date=2020-11-02|lang=en}}</ref> Security forces also used flash grenades, tear gas and batons to disperse the crowds. Some motorists tried to block the movement of vehicles intended to carry off detainees.<ref name=11-01>{{Cite news|url=https://www.rferl.org/a/belarus-forces-fire-tear-gas-beat-demonstrators-in-minsk-as-tens-of-thousands-take-to-streets/30924193.html|title=Belarus Forces Fire Tear Gas, Beat Demonstrators In Minsk As Tens Of Thousands Take To Streets|work=Radio Free Europe|date=2020-11-01|access-date=2020-11-02|lang=en}}</ref> The Interior Ministry of Belarus said that about 300 people were detained in Minsk and the Minsk region for breaking laws on mass gatherings. Four journalists were among those detained on 1 November, two of whom were severely beaten. The [[Investigative Committee of Belarus|Investigative Committee]] said 231 of those arrested were recognized as suspects in a criminal case that had been opened into "actions that grossly violate public order."<ref name=11-02>{{Cite news|url=https://www.rferl.org/a/belarus-says-300-detained-during-opposition-protests-two-journalists-reportedly-severely-beaten-/30925812.html|title=Belarusian Pensioners Take To Minsk Streets After Hundreds Of Protesters Detained|work=Radio Free Europe|date=2020-11-02|access-date=2020-11-04|lang=en}}</ref> 1 November marked the "13th Sunday" of the 2020 Belarusian protests. The protesters demanded the resignation of President [[Alexander Lukashenko]]. The President allegedly used security forces to stop demonstrators from gathering and warned that his government "would not back down."<ref name="dw_11-01"/>

On 2 November, more than 1,000 demonstrators took part in a march in Minsk. Many of them were pensioners. They carried the banned [[Flag_of_Belarus#White-red-white_flag|white-red-white flags]] and chanted slogans such as "Lukashenka! Tribunal!" and "Until victory, until the end!" during the march. No detentions were reported during the Monday protest.<ref name="11-02"/>

On 7 November, hundreds of people took part in a women's march.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://apnews.com/article/alexander-lukashenko-belarus-elections-arrests-minsk-1cfcd55f31ee2f07a7fab4500f536900|title=Dozens arrested at latest Belarus election, police protests|work=Associated Press|date=2020-11-08|access-date=2020-11-10|lang=en}}</ref> About 60 doctors and other health-care workers gathered against Lukashenka were taken away to police stations. At least 14 people were detained at the women's march in Minsk.<ref name=11-08 />

On 8 November, several thousand people marched in Minsk. Participants in the March waved red-and-white flags and umbrellas. Security forces blocked several streets and cordoned off areas in central Minsk. Access to the Internet was restricted in Minsk since the morning. Several subway stations in the city center closed an hour before the rally, citing "passenger safety." Police used batons and rubber bullets to disperse the crowds. At least 1,053 protesters were detained in Minsk, Homel, Vitebsk, Zhlobin, and other cities. At least nine of those listed as detained were journalists. Video and photos showed that unmarked men brutally wrestling demonstrators to the ground and forcing them into police transport.<ref name=11-08>{{Cite news|url=https://www.rferl.org/a/belarusian-activists-say-more-than-500-detained-at-anti-government-rallies/30936279.html|title=Belarusian Activists Say More Than 800 Detained At Anti-Government Rallies|work=Radio Free Europe|date=2020-11-08|access-date=2020-11-09|lang=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://spring96.org/en/news/100313|title=Over 1,000 protesters detained amid violent dispersals|work=[[Vyasna]]|date=2020-11-09|access-date=2020-11-09}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.amnesty.org/en/latest/news/2020/11/belarus-more-than-1000-people-arrested-in-a-single-day-of-peaceful-protests-amid-escalating-repression-of-rights/|title=Belarus: More than 1,000 people arrested in a single day of peaceful protests amid escalating repression of rights|work=[[Amnesty International]]|date=2020-11-09|access-date=2020-11-10}}</ref>

On 23 November, the "March of Wisdom" took place in Minsk, several thousand elderly citizens marched. When passing through the [[State Security Committee of the Republic of Belarus|KGB]] building, protesters chanted "Congratulations!" to greet ex-presidential candidate Viktor Babariko. Law enforcement officers accompanied the group along the route of the march, but they did not try to stop the rally.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://tass.com/world/1221557|title=Senior citizens attend rally in support of protesters in Minsk without incidents|work=[[TASS]]|date=2020-11-10|access-date=2020-12-05|lang=en}}</ref>

On 13 November, thousands of people rallied in Minsk and other Belarusian cities following the death of a 31-year-old opposition supporter who reportedly was beaten by security forces. Participants carrying flowers and candles formed human chains of solidarity to honor the late opposition supporter, [[Raman Bandarenka]], who died at a Minsk hospital after several hours of surgery for serious injuries.<ref>{{Cite web |url=https://www.amnesty.org/en/latest/news/2020/11/belarus-peaceful-protester-held-by-police-after-beating-dies-in-hospital/|title=Belarus: Peaceful protester held by police after beating dies in hospital|work=[[Amnesty International]]|date=2020-11-13|access-date=2020-11-14}}</ref> Some of the banners the demonstrators held said, "Stop killing us." In a video from the courtyard where Bondarenko was detained, hundreds of people stood in a minute of silence on Friday and then chanted: "We will not forget, we will not forgive." The [[Ministry of Internal Affairs (Belarus)|Ministry of Internal Affairs]] denied responsibility for Bondarenko's death, saying he was killed due to a scuffle with civilians.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.aljazeera.com/news/2020/11/13/outrage-in-belarus-eu-after-opposition-supporter-dies|title=Outrage in Belarus, EU after opposition supporter dies|work=Al Jazeera|date=2020-11-13|access-date=2020-11-14|lang=en}}</ref> The European Union condemned the violent crackdown.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://apnews.com/article/alexander-lukashenko-belarus-europe-265b41751fd044271118295ceab0a91b|title=Outrage in Belarus, EU after opposition supporter death|work=Associated Press|date=2020-11-13|access-date=2020-11-14|lang=en}}</ref>

[[File:2020 Belarusian protests, Minsk, 15 November v7.webm|thumb|right|AMAP/OMON troopers arresting and beating protesters. Minsk, 15 November]]
On 15 November, tens of thousands of Belarusians gathered across Belarus protested against the death in police custody of a military veteran and children‚Äôs art teacher arrested for his opposition to Lukashenko.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/2020/nov/15/belarus-thousands-protest-against-death-of-teacher-in-police-custody|title=Belarus: thousands protest against death of teacher in police custody|author=Andrew Roth|work=The Guardian|date=2020-11-15|access-date=2020-11-15|lang=en}}</ref> Demonstrators in Minsk carried the banned [[Flag_of_Belarus#White-red-white_flag|white-red-white flags]] flags and chanted slogans like, "Lukashenka! Tribunal!" and "Love live Belarus!" The security forces used tear gas, rubber bullets, stun grenades and batons to disperse the demonstrators in Minsk.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-54953599|title=Belarus: 'Over 1,000 arrested' at latest anti-government protest|work=BBC News|date=2020-11-16|access-date=2020-11-18|lang=en}}</ref> Mobile Internet was down in Minsk and several subway stations in central Minsk were closed. More than 1,200 protesters were detained in Minsk and other cities, including in Homel, Hrodna, and Mogilev.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.rferl.org/a/belarusian-police-detain-dozens-of-protesters/30951057.html|title=More Than 1,200 Detained In Belarus As Protesters Face Tear Gas, Stun Grenades|work=Radio Free Europe|date=2020-11-15|access-date=2020-11-18|lang=en}}</ref><ref>{{cite web |script-title=be:–ó–∞—Ç—Ä—ã–º–∞–Ω–Ω—ñ –Ω–∞ –∞–∫—Ü—ã—è—Ö –ø—Ä–∞—Ç—ç—Å—Ç—É 15 –ª—ñ—Å—Ç–∞–ø–∞–¥–∞ |url=http://spring96.org/be/news/100425 |date=2020-11-15|access-date=2020-11-18|work=[[Viasna Human Rights Centre]] |language=be}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=http://spring96.org/en/news/100429|title=Over 1,000 detained again in Sunday protests|work=[[Viasna Human Rights Centre]]|date=2020-11-16|access-date=2020-11-18|lang=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://edition.cnn.com/videos/world/2020/11/16/minsk-belarus-protests-arrests-lukashenko-newsroom-intl-ldn-vpx.cnn|title=Video shows Belarus police beating protesters inside supermarket|publisher=[[CNN]]|date=2020-11-16|access-date=2020-11-19|lang=en}}</ref>

On 16 November, the "March of Sorrow" took place in Minsk, more than 2,000 people marched. Many of them were pensioners and medics. They chanted slogans such as "Murderers!" and "Tribunal!" during the march. Authorities blocked central [[Independence Square, Minsk|Independence Square]] and nearby streets while several subway stations were closed. No detentions were reported.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.rferl.org/a/elderly-in-belarus-demand-justice-for-slain-anti-government-protester/30953227.html|title=Elderly in Belarus Demand Justice For Slain Anti-Government Protester|work=Radio Free Europe|date=2020-11-16|access-date=2020-11-21|lang=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.foxnews.com/world/belarus-socialism-legacy-lukashenko-protests-police-violence|title=Legacy of socialism? State violence continues in Belarus|author=Danielle Wallace|publisher=Fox News|date=2020-11-19|access-date=2020-11-21|lang=en}}</ref>

On 22 November, tens of thousands of people gathered in several places around Minsk, chanting "Long live Belarus!" and carrying signs and the [[Flag_of_Belarus#White-red-white_flag|white-red-white flags]]. Protesters gathered in residential areas and then came together in Minsk to avoid getting shut down early by police. Several metro stations were closed and communications were cut at times. Outside one subway station in central Minsk, demonstrators were met with flashbang grenades. Masked and balaclava-wearing officers ripped flags from some people's hands in another location. Security forces deployed heavily around Minsk with armored vehicles and water cannons before the rally. At least 379 protesters were detained in Minsk and other cities of Belarus. At least 13 detained protesters were taken to hospitals after they were beaten by riot police and other security forces involved in dispersing the protests.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.rferl.org/a/anti-government-protesters-rally-in-belarusian-capital/30963034.html|title=Hundreds Detained Despite New Tack By Anti-Government Protesters In Belarus|work=Radio Free Europe|date=2020-11-22|access-date=2020-11-23|lang=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.dw.com/en/belarus-thousands-continue-anti-president-protests-in-minsk/a-55691899|title=Belarus: Thousands continue anti-president protests in Minsk|work=Deutsche Welle|date=2020-11-22|access-date=2020-11-23|lang=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=http://spring96.org/en/news/100429|title=380 detained on Day 106 of post-election protests|work=[[Viasna Human Rights Centre]]|date=2020-11-23|access-date=2020-11-23|lang=en}}</ref> 

The [[Belarusian Autocephalous Orthodox Church]] (not to be confused with the [[Belarusian Orthodox Church]]) announced an [[anathema]] against Lukashenko, publicly declaring him an "executioner of the Belarusian people".<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.rferl.org/a/minor-belarusian-emigrant-church-declares-lukashenka-anathema-/30963469.html|title=Minor Belarusian Emigrant Church Declares Lukashenka 'Anathema'|work=Radio Free Europe|date=2020-11-22|access-date=2020-11-25|lang=en}}</ref>

On 23 November, the "March of Wisdom" took place in Minsk, several thousand pensioners marched. They carried the [[Flag_of_Belarus#White-red-white_flag|white-red-white flags]] and shouted "Freedom for political prisoners!" and "Murderers!". Black-clad security forces wearing balaclavas blocked the columns of elderly protesters to prevent them from entering [[Independence Avenue (Minsk)|Independence Avenue]]. At least six people were detained, including two elderly women in their 70s, who were later released. Minor scuffles were reported, with witnesses saying security forces pushed several of the elderly onto the asphalt.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.rferl.org/a/minor-scuffles-with-police-as-elderly-march-in-support-of-belarus-s-democracy-movement/30965771.html|title=Minor Scuffles With Police As Elderly March In Support Of Belarus's Democracy Movement|work=Radio Free Europe|date=2020-11-24|access-date=2020-11-25|lang=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/belarus-pensioners-march-demanding-leaders-resignation/2020/11/23/cc46f6d6-2da5-11eb-9dd6-2d0179981719_story.html|title=Belarus pensioners march demanding leader's resignation|agency=Associated Press|date=2020-11-24|access-date=2020-11-27|lang=en}}</ref>

On 24 November, a well known [[anarchist]] organizer and protester [[Mikalai Dzyadok]], was arrested. According to Mikalai he was forcefully taken from his residence by police. He claims he was beaten by the police who attempted to get information to anarchist activities, after refusing the Police sprayed Mikalai. He claimed he was batoned, kicked and stun-gunned and pepper sprayed and forced to make a confession on video. Mikalai face can be seen badly beaten while making the confession he can be seen with a black eye.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://belsat.eu/en/news/anarchist-movement-activist-dzyadok-charged/|title=Anarchist movement activist Dzyadok charged|work=Belsat TV|date=2020-11-24|access-date=2020-11-27}}</ref> While in custody Mikalai was threatened with [[rape]] and [[murder]]. Authorities state that Mikalai is being charged for organizing multiple mass protests and [[riots]] in Belarus, Mikalai denies these accusations, he is currently held as a [[political prisoner]].<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://belsat.eu/en/news/arrested-activist-dzyadok-teargassed-threatened-with-rape-stifled-with-pillow/|title=Arrested activist Dzyadok tear-gassed, threatened with rape, stifled with pillow|work=Belsat TV|date=2020-11-25|access-date=2020-11-27}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://naviny.belsat.eu/en/news/activist-mikalai-dziadok-fined-for-illegal-political-activity/|title=Activist Mikalai Dziadok fined for 'illegal' political activity|work=Belsat TV|date=2019-03-08|access-date=2020-11-27}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://belsat.eu/en/news/belsat-tut-by-journos-andreyeva-chultsova-barysevich-recognised-as-prisoners-of-conscience/|title=Belsat, TUT.BY journos Andreyeva, Chultsova, Barysevich recognised as prisoners of conscience|work=Belsat TV|date=2020-11-24|access-date=2020-11-27}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://secoursrouge.org/bielorussie-arrestation-dun-ancien-prisonnier-anarchiste/|title=Bi√©lorussie: Arrestation d'un ancien prisonnier anarchiste|work=Secours Rouge|date=2020-03-30|access-date=2020-11-27|lang=fr}}</ref>

On 29 November, the "March of Neighbors" took place in Minsk. They carried the [[Flag_of_Belarus#White-red-white_flag|white-red-white flags]] and chanted "Go away, rat!", referring to Lukashenko. The opposition adopted the strategy as a way of decentralizing the protests and making it more difficult for police to round up activists. At least 20 protests took place in Minsk. In some areas, separate rallies merged to form columns of several hundred people. Police deployed tear gas and stun grenades to break up some of the crowds in Minsk, and some were chased into residential courtyards and beaten with Batons. Before the rally, water cannon, armored vehicles and police vans were seen in the center of Minsk. Mobile Internet services were not available in Minsk and the central metro stations were closed. There were also reports of power cuts in some neighborhoods. At least 416 protesters were detained in Minsk, Brest, Hrodno, Barauliany, and other cities. Six persons were reportedly taken to hospitals after being beaten by riot police and other law enforcement officers. Two journalists were detained despite carrying valid press IDs.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.rferl.org/a/belarus-dozens-detained-anti-lukashenka-marches/30974817.html|title=More Than 300 Reported Detained In Belarus At Anti-Lukashenka Marches|work=Radio Free Europe|date=2020-11-29|access-date=2020-11-30|lang=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.dw.com/en/belarus-protesters-gather-in-minsk-districts-hundreds-arrested/a-55764349|title=Belarus protesters gather in Minsk districts, hundreds arrested|work=Deutsche Welle|date=2020-11-29|access-date=2020-11-30|lang=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=http://spring96.org/en/news/100429|title=Day 113 of protests: over 400 detained|work=[[Viasna]]|date=2020-11-30|access-date=2020-11-30|lang=en}}</ref>

On 30 November, the "March of Wisdom" took place in Minsk, more than 1,000 pensioners marched, chanting 'Shame!', 'Grandmas and grandpas, let‚Äôs march to the victory!', 'Long live Belarus!'. Police blocked the protesters along their planned route, divided them into smaller groups. At least 20 people were detained.<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.rferl.org/a/belarusian-pensioners-detained-during-protest-as-crackdowns-continue/30976283.html|title=Belarusian Pensioners Detained During Protest As Crackdowns Continue|work=Radio Free Europe|date=2020-11-30|access-date=2020-12-01|lang=en}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|script-title=be:–ó–∞—Ç—Ä—ã–º–∞–Ω–Ω—ñ –Ω–∞ –ú–∞—Ä—à—ã. –•—Ä–æ–Ω—ñ–∫–∞ –ø–µ—Ä–∞—Å–ª–µ–¥—É 30 –ª—ñ—Å—Ç–∞–ø–∞–¥–∞|url=https://spring96.org/be/news/100691|date=2020-11-30|access-date=2020-12-01|work=[[Viasna Human Rights Centre]] |language=be}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://belsat.eu/en/news/seniors-protesting-in-minsk-grandmas-and-grandpas-let-s-march-to-the-victory/|title=Seniors protesting in Minsk: ‚ÄòGrandmas and grandpas, let‚Äôs march to the victory!‚Äô|work=Belsat TV|date=2020-11-30|access-date=2020-12-05}}</ref>

===December===
On 1 December, Sviatlana Tsikhanouskaya said in a video call from Vilnius, Lithuania, that the "book of crimes" will include accounts of police abuse that will be verified by independent lawyers. "Impunity will not last forever," said Tsikhanouskaya. "No one will be able to deprive hundreds of thousands of people who are striving for justice from speaking out."<ref>{{Cite news|url=https://apnews.com/article/alexander-lukashenko-belarus-sviatlana-tsikhanouskaya-lithuania-elections-89192d64176437fc7663b3e7ddec92c0|title=Belarus opposition to compile 'book of crimes'|work=Associated Press|date=2020-12-01|access-date=2020-12-02|lang=en}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|url=https://www.euronews.com/2020/12/01/belarus-opposition-to-compile-register-of-alleged-police-abuses|title=Belarus opposition to compile register of alleged police abuses|work=Euronews|date=2020-12-01|access-date=2020-12-02|lang=en}}</ref>

==Coordination Council and NAM==
{{main|Coordination Council|National Anti-crisis Management}}
[[File:First press conference of the Coordination Council of Belarus.jpg|thumb|left|First press conference of the Coordination Council on 18 August 2020]]
On 14 August, in a video in which Tsikhanouskaya claimed that she had received 60{{Ndash}}70% of the vote, she announced the creation of the [[Coordination Council (Belarus)|Coordination Council for the Transfer of Power]].<ref name="BBC148"/>

Tsikhanouskaya stated that the council should be made of "civil society activists, respected Belarusians and professionals" to handle the transfer of power from Lukashenko.<ref name="BBC148"/><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www3.nhk.or.jp/nhkworld/en/news/20200815_05/amp.html?__twitter_impression=true|title=Belarus opposition candidate declares victory &#124; NHK WORLD-JAPAN News|website=www3.nhk.or.jp}}</ref> Applications for membership of the transitional council were open to any Belarusian citizen who recognised the election as having been falsified, and who was in a position of social trust such as a doctor, a teacher, a business leader, an author or a sportsperson.<ref name="OKOpress_council_conditions"/>

On 17 August, Tsikhanouskaya released a video in which she stated that she is ready to lead a transitional government<ref name="auto3"/><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.euronews.com/2020/08/17/belarus-tsikhanouskaya-says-she-s-ready-to-become-national-leader|title=Thousands rally in Minsk as EU prepares emergency summit on Belarus|date=17 August 2020|website=euronews}}</ref> and to organise a new, free and fair [[Next Belarusian presidential election|presidential election]].<ref name="auto6"/> A list of members was circulated on 17 August 2020 and included Nobel Prize laureate [[Svetlana Alexievich]].<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://rada.vision/nazvany-pervye-chleny-koordinatsionnogo-soveta|title=–ù–∞–∑–≤–∞–Ω—ã –ø–µ—Ä–≤—ã–µ —á–ª–µ–Ω—ã –ö–æ–æ—Ä–¥–∏–Ω–∞—Ü–∏–æ–Ω–Ω–æ–≥–æ –°–æ–≤–µ—Ç–∞|date=17 August 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.facebook.com/KavalkovaVolya/posts/1662270923930444|title=–í–æ–ª—å–≥–∞ –ö–∞–≤–∞–ª—å–∫–æ–≤–∞|website=www.facebook.com}}</ref> The first meeting of the Council took place on 18 August and its leadership was elected the following day.<ref>{{Cite news |title=–í –æ—Ä–≥–∞–Ω–∏–∑–æ–≤–∞–Ω–Ω–æ–º –¢–∏—Ö–∞–Ω–æ–≤—Å–∫–æ–π –∫–æ–æ—Ä–¥–∏–Ω–∞—Ü–∏–æ–Ω–Ω–æ–º —Å–æ–≤–µ—Ç–µ –ø–æ –ø–µ—Ä–µ–¥–∞—á–µ –≤–ª–∞—Å—Ç–∏ –Ω–∞–∑–≤–∞–ª–∏ –¥–∞—Ç—É –ø–µ—Ä–≤–æ–π –≤—Å—Ç—Ä–µ—á–∏ |url= https://tvrain.ru/news/v_organizovannom_tihanovskoj_koordinatsionnom_sovete_po_peredache_vlasti_nazvali_datu_pervoj_vstrechi-514522/ |website=–∫–∞–Ω–∞–ª –î–æ–∂–¥—å |date=17 August 2020}}</ref>

Lukashenko decried the creation of the council as an 'attempt to seize power' and promised "appropriate measures".<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.reuters.com/article/us-belarus-election/belarus-opposition-sets-up-council-lukashenko-decries-attempt-to-seize-power-idUSKCN25E16F |title=Belarus opposition sets up council; Lukashenko decries 'attempt to seize power' |last=Makhovsky |first=Andrei |publisher=Reuters |date=18 August 2020}}</ref> On 20 August the chief prosecutor launched a criminal case against the council, calling it unconstitutional.<ref name="BBC218"/> 

[[United States Secretary of State]], [[Mike Pompeo]], in a statement urged the Belarusian government to actively engage Belarusian society, including through the newly established Coordination Council, "in a way that reflects what the Belarusian people are demanding, for the sake of Belarus‚Äô future, and for a successful Belarus."<ref name="Pompeo_20_August_statement">{{cite web |url=https://www.state.gov/supporting-the-aspirations-of-the-belarusian-people/ |title=Supporting the Aspirations of the Belarusian People |publisher=US Department of State |date=20 August 2020}}</ref>

[[Dmitry Peskov]], spokesperson for Russian [[President of Russia|President]] [[Vladimir Putin]] welcomed the fact that the leadership of the Coordination Council did not want to reduce their ties with Russia and instead hoped to continue with good bilateral relationships between the two countries.<ref>{{Cite web|title=–ü–µ—Å–∫–æ–≤ –æ—Ü–µ–Ω–∏–ª –∑–∞—è–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ –±–µ–ª–æ—Ä—É—Å—Å–∫–æ–π –æ–ø–ø–æ–∑–∏—Ü–∏–∏ –æ —Å–æ—Ç—Ä—É–¥–Ω–∏—á–µ—Å—Ç–≤–µ —Å –†–æ—Å—Å–∏–µ–π|url=https://www.rbc.ru/rbcfreenews/5f44e4039a79474f8dd12795|access-date=28 August 2020|website=–†–ë–ö|language=ru}}</ref> 

On 17 September, the [[European Parliament]] recognized the coordination council as the "interim representation of the people" of Belarus.<ref>https://www.europarl.europa.eu/news/en/press-room/20200910IPR86829/meps-call-for-eu-sanctions-against-belarusian-president-and-navalny-s-poisoners</ref>

In late October, the Coordination Council created a shadow government, called ''[[National Anti-crisis Management]]'' (NAM), for organising the detailed administrative tasks for a peaceful transfer of power to a fairly and freely elected president.<ref name="BelFeed_NAU_created" /><ref name="CEPA_NAM_created" /> NAM is led by Pavel Latushko and states that it will [[sunset clause|lose its powers]] when a new president is inaugurated.<ref name="NAM_homepage_en_20201116" /> In November, NAM published internal reports from the Belarusian [[Ministry of Internal Affairs (Belarus)|Ministry of Internal Affairs]] showing that 4000 complaints for torture and other illegal actions by security forces had been submitted between 9 August and 9 November but all had been ignored by the ministry.<ref name="OKOpress_Bandarenka_NAU" />

==Deaths==
[[File:–ú–∏—Ç–∏–Ω–≥ –ø–∞–º—è—Ç–∏ –ê–ª–µ–∫—Å–∞–Ω–¥—Ä–∞ –¢–∞—Ä–∞–π–∫–æ–≤—Å–∫–æ–≥–æ, –º–µ—Ç—Ä–æ –ü—É—à–∫–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∞—è, –ú–∏–Ω—Å–∫, 15 –∞–≤–≥—É—Å—Ç–∞ 2020 133.jpg|thumb|Rally in memory of [[Alexander Taraikovsky]] on 15 August]]
[[File:–ú–∏—Ç–∏–Ω–≥ –ø–∞–º—è—Ç–∏ –ê–ª–µ–∫—Å–∞–Ω–¥—Ä–∞ –¢–∞—Ä–∞–π–∫–æ–≤—Å–∫–æ–≥–æ, –º–µ—Ç—Ä–æ –ü—É—à–∫–∏–Ω—Å–∫–∞—è, –ú–∏–Ω—Å–∫, 15 –∞–≤–≥—É—Å—Ç–∞ 2020 265.jpg|thumb|upright=0.81|Makeshift board with photographs and a drawing of a dead OMON on a gallows, holding a bloody stick.]]
On 10 August, a protester, [[Alexander Taraikovsky]], died near [[Pushkinskaya (Minsk Metro)|Pushkinskaya metro station]]. According to the Ministry of Internal Affairs, the protester tried to throw an explosive device at the government troopers and it exploded in his arms.<ref name=t.t2/><ref name=dw>[https://www.dw.com/ru/v-minske-pri-vzryve-pogib-demonstrant/a-54521233 –í –ú–∏–Ω—Å–∫–µ –ø—Ä–∏ –≤–∑—Ä—ã–≤–µ –ø–æ–≥–∏–± –¥–µ–º–æ–Ω—Å—Ç—Ä–∞–Ω—Ç].
