AP –æ–ø—É–±–ª–∏–∫–æ–≤–∞–ª–æ –∫–∞–¥—Ä –∏–∑ –≤–∏–¥–µ–æ —Å –≥–∏–±–µ–ª—å—é –ê–ª–µ–∫—Å–∞–Ω–¥—Ä–∞ –¢–∞—Ä–∞–π–∫–æ–≤—Å–∫–æ–≥–æ –Ω–∞ ¬´–ü—É—à–∫–∏–Ω—Å–∫–æ–π¬ª]. ''[[Tut.by]]''. Retrieved on 15 August 2020.</ref> Elena German, the wife of Taraikovsky, saw the body in the morgue and reported that there were no injuries to his hands, but there was a small hole in his chest, consistent with a bullet hole.<ref name="euro158">{{cite news |url=https://www.euronews.com/2020/08/15/lukashenko-calls-putin-as-demonstrators-gather-once-again-in-belarus |title=Lukashenko calls Putin as demonstrators gather once again in Belarus |publisher=euronews |last=Hurst |first=Luke |date=15 August 2020}}</ref> On 15 August, thousands of people gathered at the funeral in Minsk.<ref name=t.t/><ref>[https://www.rferl.org/a/belarus-postelection-massive-weekend-protests/30785061.html Thousands Mourn Protester As Belarus's Postelection Rallies Continue]. ''[[Radio Liberty]]/Free Europe''. Retrieved on 15 August 2020.</ref>

On 12 August, 25-year-old Alexander Vikhor died in Gomel. He is believed to have had a heart-related disease. According to preliminary information, he died because of waiting in a security forces detainee van for many hours in hot weather. He was in the van because the city's temporary detention centres were overcrowded. He was sentenced to 10 days in prison but wasn't given proper medical attention in time.<ref name="auto5"/><ref>{{Cite web|title="–ú–Ω–µ –∞–¥–º–æ–≤—ñ–ª—ñ—Å—è –ø–∞–∫–∞–∑–≤–∞—Ü—å —Ü–µ–ª–∞ —Å—ã–Ω–∞". –£ –ì–æ–º–ª—ñ –ø–∞—Å—å–ª—è –∑–∞—Ç—Ä—ã–º–∞–Ω—å–Ω—è –ø–∞–º—ë—Ä 25-–≥–∞–¥–æ–≤—ã —Ö–ª–æ–ø–µ—Ü|url=https://www.svaboda.org/a/30780258.html|access-date=12 August 2020|website=–†–∞–¥—ã—ë –°–≤–∞–±–æ–¥–∞|language=be}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|last=|first=|date=12 August 2020|title="–ú–æ–π —Å—ã–Ω –Ω–µ —É–º–µ—Ä, –æ–Ω –ø–æ–≥–∏–± –Ω–∏ –∑–∞ —á—Ç–æ". –í –ì–æ–º–µ–ª–µ —Å–∫–æ–Ω—á–∞–ª—Å—è 25-–ª–µ—Ç–Ω–∏–π –ø–∞—Ä–µ–Ω—å, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–≥–æ –∑–∞–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∞–ª–∏ –Ω–∞ —É–ª–∏—Ü–µ|url=https://news.tutby.news/society/696437.html|url-status=live|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200812211711/https://news.tutby.news/society/696437.html|archive-date=12 August 2012|access-date=12 August 2020|website=TUTBY.NEWS|language=ru}}</ref><ref name="BBC238">{{cite news|date=13 August 2020|title=Belarus election: Second protester dies as UN sounds alarm|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-europe-53760453}}</ref>

Also on or about 12 August, 28-year-old Nikita Krivtsov disappeared. His body was found on 22 August near Minsk. Krivtsov was a fan of [[FC Molodechno]], whose home ground is in the city of [[Maladzyechna]]. On 9 August, the day of the election, there was a peaceful protest in Maladzyechna against the official election result. Photographs show Krivtsov at the front of the protest, carrying a white-red-white flag, confronting a line of police. A friend says that Krivtsov phoned him on 10 August, stating that he was in Minsk and had nearly been arrested by riot police. The friend says Krivtsov phoned him again on 11 August saying that he spent much of the day in a bar. On 12 August the friend tried phoning Krivtsov but got no answer, which he said was out of character.<ref name=Krivtsov/> Another report suggests that on 12 August Krivtsov was in the city of [[Zhodzina]], where his estranged wife lives with their five-year-old daughter, and that he left Zhodzina to go to the village of Korolev Stan, where he worked, but he never arrived.<ref>{{cite news |url= https://news.tut.by/society/697905.html |last=Borisevich |first=Katerina |title="–°–µ–º—å—è –Ω–µ –≤–µ—Ä–∏—Ç, —á—Ç–æ —É—à–µ–ª –∏–∑ –∂–∏–∑–Ω–∏ —Å–∞–º". –†–æ–¥–Ω—ã–µ –ù–∏–∫–∏—Ç—ã –ö—Ä–∏–≤—Ü–æ–≤–∞ –Ω–∞–ø–∏—Å–∞–ª–∏ –∑–∞—è–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ –≤ –°–ö |language=ru |website=[[Tut.By]] |date=24 August 2020 |accessdate=25 September 2020}}</ref> On 22 August a watchman found Krivtsov's body in a forest near Minsk. The body was hanging by the neck but its feet were on the ground. The condition of the body suggested that Krivtsov had been dead for about a week. Police claim that Krivtsov committed suicide, but his family do not believe them.<ref name=Krivtsov/>

On 15 August, 29-year-old [[Konstantin Shishmakov]] ([[Belarusian language|Belarussian]]: Kanstantsin Shyshmakou), director of the [[Operation Bagration|Bagration]] Military History Museum in [[Vawkavysk]], disappeared. As a member of the election commission, he refused to sign the protocols, called his wife at about 5 pm and said: "I will not work here anymore, I am going home." But he never came home. Later he was found dead in a river. This was announced by the search and rescue squad "Angel".<ref>{{Cite web|date=18 August 2020|title=–î–∏—Ä–µ–∫—Ç–æ—Ä–∞ –≤–æ–ª–∫–æ–≤—ã—Å—Å–∫–æ–≥–æ –º—É–∑–µ—è –Ω–∞—à–ª–∏ –º–µ—Ä—Ç–≤—ã–º|url=https://news.tut.by/society/697178.html|access-date=18 August 2020|website=TUT.BY|language=ru}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|date=19 August 2020|title=Museum director from Vaukavysk found dead|url=https://www.voiceofbelarus.com/lt/2020-08-19/museum-director-from-vaukavysk-found-dead/|access-date=21 August 2020|website=Voice of Belarus|language=lt-LT}}</ref>

On 17 August, the [[Human rights defender|human rights advocates]] from the Belarusian education and social association "Zvyano" ("Link") issued a report, which said that at least five people had been murdered during the protests, and seven people were in critical medical condition.<ref>{{Cite web|title=–ü—Ä–∞–≤–æ–∑–∞—â–∏—Ç–Ω–∏–∫–∏: –ù–∞ —É–ª–∏—á–Ω—ã—Ö –ø—Ä–æ—Ç–µ—Å—Ç–∞—Ö –≤ –ë–µ–ª–∞—Ä—É—Å–∏ —É–±–∏–ª–∏ –∫–∞–∫ –º–∏–Ω–∏–º—É–º –ø—è—Ç–µ—Ä—ã—Ö. –°–µ–º–µ—Ä–æ ‚Äì –≤ –∫—Ä–∏—Ç–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–æ–º —Å–æ—Å—Ç–æ—è–Ω–∏–∏ |trans-title=Human rights defenders: At least five people were killed in street protests in Belarus. Seven are in critical condition. |url=https://gordonua.com/news/localnews/pravozashchitniki-na-ulichnyh-protestah-v-belarusi-ubili-kak-minimum-pyateryh-semero-v-kriticheskom-sostoyanii-1514059.html|access-date=17 August 2020|website=gordonua.com}}</ref><ref name=":8">{{Cite web|last=|first=|date=17 August 2020|title=–î–æ–∫–ª–∞–¥ –æ –Ω–∞—Ä—É—à–µ–Ω–∏–∏ –ø—Ä–∞–≤ —á–µ–ª–æ–≤–µ–∫–∞ —É—á–∞—Å—Ç–Ω–∏–∫–æ–≤ –ø—Ä–æ—Ç–µ—Å—Ç–æ–≤ –≤ –ë–µ–ª–∞—Ä—É—Å–∏ —Å 7 –ø–æ 14 –∞–≤–≥—É—Å—Ç–∞ 2020 –≥–æ–¥–∞|trans-title=Report on violation of human rights of protesters in Belarus from 7 to 14 August 2020|url=http://zvyano.by/–¥–æ–∫–ª–∞–¥-–æ-–Ω–∞—Ä—É—à–µ–Ω–∏–∏-–ø—Ä–∞–≤-—É—á–∞—Å—Ç–Ω–∏–∫–æ–≤-–ø—Ä/|url-status=live|archive-url=|archive-date=|access-date=18 August 2020|website=Zvyano (Link)}}</ref>

On 19 August, 43-year-old Gennady Shutov died in the Minsk military hospital after he had received a gunshot to his head during the 11 August protests in Brest; reportedly, the shot was fired by the police.<ref>{{Cite web|date=19 August 2020|title=–í –≥–æ—Å–ø–∏—Ç–∞–ª–µ —É–º–µ—Ä –º—É–∂—á–∏–Ω–∞ –∏–∑ –ë—Ä–µ—Å—Ç–∞, –≤ –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–≥–æ —Å–∏–ª–æ–≤–∏–∫–∏ –≤—ã—Å—Ç—Ä–µ–ª–∏–ª–∏ –Ω–∞ –ø—Ä–æ—Ç–µ—Å—Ç–∞—Ö. –ï–º—É –±—ã–ª–æ 43 –≥–æ–¥–∞|url=https://news.tut.by/society/697248.html|access-date=19 August 2020|website=TUT.BY|language=ru}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|date=20 August 2020|title=Third Belarus protester's death reported|publisher=Yarrawonga Chronicle|url=https://www.yarrawongachronicle.com.au/world/2020/08/20/1523805/third-belarus-protesters-death-reported}}</ref>

On 3 October, Denis Kuznetsov, a 41-year-old male who was detained on 29 September, died in an [[intensive care unit]] after being transported there from Okrestina. According to Kuznetsov's relatives and his [[medical history]], during transportation to the hospital, he informed the medics that he was beaten by the Okrestina staff, who, in turn, claimed that Kuznetsov "fell from the top of a [[bunk bed]]". The Kuznetsov's clinical diagnosis, among other things, included [[Traumatic_brain_injury#Severity|moderate traumatic brain injury]], numerous [[hematoma]]s, [[basilar skull fracture]], [[subarachnoid hemorrhage]] and [[Rib fracture|fractures]] of 11 right [[rib]]s.<ref name="kyky_Kuznetsov_diagnosis">{{cite web |url=https://kyky.org/news/skazal-vracham-chto-bili-siloviki-umer-muzhchina-kotorogo-privezli-iz-okrestina-v-bolnitsu-s-cherepno-mozgovoy-i-perelomami-reber |title="–°–∫–∞–∑–∞–ª, —á—Ç–æ –±–∏–ª–∏ —Å–∏–ª–æ–≤–∏–∫–∏". –£–º–µ—Ä –º—É–∂—á–∏–Ω–∞, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–≥–æ –ø—Ä–∏–≤–µ–∑–ª–∏ –∏–∑ –û–∫—Ä–µ—Å—Ç–∏–Ω–∞ –≤ –±–æ–ª—å–Ω–∏—Ü—É —Å —á–µ—Ä–µ–ø–Ω–æ-–º–æ–∑–≥–æ–≤–æ–π –∏ –ø–µ—Ä–µ–ª–æ–º–∞–º–∏ —Ä–µ–±–µ—Ä |date=3 October 2020 |access-date=3 October 2020 |website=kyky.org |language=ru }}</ref><ref name="Belsat_Kuznetsov_death">{{cite news |url=https://belsat.eu/news/zbity-na-akrestsina-dzyanis-k-syonnya-pamyor/ |title=–ó–±—ñ—Ç—ã –Ω–∞ –ê–∫—Ä—ç—Å—Ü—ñ–Ω–∞ –î–∑—è–Ω—ñ—Å –ö. —Å—ë–Ω–Ω—è –ø–∞–º—ë—Ä |date=3 October 2020 |access-date=3 October 2020 |publisher=[[Belsat TV]] |language=be }}</ref><ref name="charter_Kuznetsov_death">{{cite web |url=https://charter97.org/ru/news/2020/10/3/395579/ |title=–ò–∑–±–∏—Ç—ã–π –Ω–∞ –û–∫—Ä–µ—Å—Ç–∏–Ω–∞ –º—É–∂—á–∏–Ω–∞ —É–º–µ—Ä |date=3 October 2020 |access-date=3 October 2020 |website=charter97.org |language=ru }}</ref> In a further comment by the Belarusian Ministry of Internal Affairs, it was reported that results of the preliminary investigation supported the version presented by the Okrestina staff.<ref name="Kuznetsov_death_official_response">{{cite news |url=https://news.tut.by/society/702712.html |title="–ó–Ω–∞–µ–º, —á—Ç–æ –æ–Ω –Ω–∏ –≤ —á–µ–º –Ω–µ —É—á–∞—Å—Ç–≤–æ–≤–∞–ª". –í –ë–°–ú–ü —É–º–µ—Ä –º—É–∂—á–∏–Ω–∞, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–≥–æ –ø—Ä–∏–≤–µ–∑–ª–∏ —Ç—É–¥–∞ —Å –û–∫—Ä–µ—Å—Ç–∏–Ω–∞ |date=3 October 2020 |access-date=3 October 2020 |publisher=[[tut.by]] |language=ru }}</ref>

On 11 November, Raman Bandarenka, a 31-year-old Minsk resident, a manager and an art-designer, was attacked and kidnaped from his yard in [[Square of Changes|The Square of Changes]]. After some time, an ambulance was called to the Central District Department of Internal Affairs, which found Bandarenka unconscious. He was admitted to the intensive care unit of the Minsk BHMP (Ambulance Hospital) on November 12, 2020, at 00:05, where he was diagnosed with a severe closed traumatic brain injury, the acute subdural hematomas of the head, cerebral hemorrhage, and multiple soft tissue injuries. He was in a coma and underwent surgery, but medics were unable to save Bandarenka due to his serious condition. Bandarenka died the evening of November 12, 2020.<ref>{{Cite web|title=–ü–∞–º—ë—Ä –†–∞–º–∞–Ω –ë–∞–Ω–¥–∞—Ä—ç–Ω–∫–∞, —è–∫–æ–≥–∞ —Ö—É—Ç–∫–∞—è –∑–∞–±—Ä–∞–ª–∞ –Ω–µ–ø—Ä—ã—Ç–æ–º–Ω—ã–º –∑ –¶—ç–Ω—Ç—Ä–∞–ª—å–Ω–∞–≥–∞ –†–£–£–°|url=https://nashaniva.by/?c=ar&i=262312|access-date=2020-11-22|website=–ù–∞—à–∞ –ù—ñ–≤–∞|language=be}}</ref>

==Human rights issues==
{{main|Human rights issues related to the suppression of the 2020 Belarusian protests}}

According to numerous publications, the suppression of the 2020 Belarusian protests was accompanied by extreme police violence and systematic violation of human rights throughout stages of the detention process.<ref name=":1"/><ref name=":5"/><ref name=":9"/><ref name=":10"/><ref name=":11"/><ref name=":12"/><ref name=":13"/><ref name=":14"/>

On 14 August, the [[World Organisation Against Torture]] (OMCT) issued a statement which condemned the arbitrary detainment and torture‚ÄØof hundreds if not thousands of protesters across Belarus following the election. According to the statement, such actions suggested [[crimes against humanity]]. The statement also called for an unbiased worldwide investigation into the "systematic and extremely violent oppression" of peaceful protests in Belarus.<ref>{{Cite web|title=Belarus: Widespread torture of protesters suggests crimes against humanity / August 14, 2020 / Statements / OMCT|url=https://www.omct.org/statements/belarus/2020/08/d26028/|access-date=18 August 2020|website=www.omct.org}}</ref>

On 19 August, the classification of these events as crimes against humanity, in accordance with the [[Rome Statute of the International Criminal Court]], was supported in a [[Human Rights Foundation]] (HRF) statement. According to the statement, HRF identified fifteen persons from the Belarusian state apparatus who were responsible for the arbitrary detention, beating and torture of thousands of peaceful protesters. Letters informing these persons of imminent criminal prosecution for crimes against humanity were sent to each of them on 17 August.<ref name="HRF_Crimes_against_humanity">{{cite web|date=19 August 2020|title=HRF Sends Letters to Belarusian Security Officers Accused of Crimes Against Humanity|url=https://hrf.org/press_posts/hrf-sends-letters-to-belarusian-security-officers-accused-of-crimes-against-humanity/|access-date=19 August 2020|website=[[Human Rights Foundation]]}}</ref> 

On 17 August, the [[Human rights defender|human rights advocates]] from the Belarusian education and social association "Zvyano" ("Link") issued the "Report on the violation of human rights of the participants in the protests in Belarus from 7 to 14 August 2020", based on interviews with 30 victims of the police abuse, as well as on interviews with doctors of several Minsk hospitals. Some of the cases were supported by audio or video evidence.<ref name=":8"/> On that same day, a statement to the Prosecutor General's Office of Belarus with request to perform an investigation of the police' actions on the basis of 16 articles of Criminal Code of Belarus, including murder, torture and rape, was issued by Viktar Babaryka's electoral campaign manager, Maria Kolesnikova.<ref name="Kolesnikova_statement">{{cite web |url=https://babariko.vision/news/zayavlenie-v-generalnuyu-prokuraturu |title=–ó–∞—è–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ –≤ –ì–µ–Ω–µ—Ä–∞–ª—å–Ω—É—é –ü—Ä–æ–∫—É—Ä–∞—Ç—É—Ä—É |date=17 August 2020 |access-date=19 August 2020 |website=babariko.vision |language=ru}}</ref>

The numerous human rights violations were confirmed and condemned by a number of former or current Belarusian police officers, such as Sergei Mikhasev, former employee of the Vitebsk police department, who was detained along with other protesters and spent several days in a detention centre in inhuman conditions,<ref>{{Cite web|date=17 August 2020|title="–ú–Ω–µ —Å—Ç—ã–¥–Ω–æ, —á—Ç–æ —è —Å–ª—É–∂–∏–ª –≤ –º–∏–ª–∏—Ü–∏–∏". –≠–∫—Å-–∑–∞–º–Ω–∞—á–∞–ª—å–Ω–∏–∫–∞ –£–í–î –∑–∞–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∞–ª–∏ –≤ –¥–µ–Ω—å –≤—ã–±–æ—Ä–æ–≤ –±—ã–≤—à–∏–µ –ø–æ–¥—á–∏–Ω–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–µ|url=https://news.tut.by/culture/696937.html|access-date=18 August 2020|website=TUT.BY|language=ru}}</ref> or Yuri Makhnach, a police officer from [[Lida]], who said that the authorities had prepared them for a war against their own people.<ref>{{Cite web|date=17 August 2020|title="–ì–æ—Ç–æ–≤–∏–ª–∏ –∫ –≤–æ–π–Ω–µ –ø—Ä–æ—Ç–∏–≤ —Å–≤–æ–µ–≥–æ –Ω–∞—Ä–æ–¥–∞". –î–µ–π—Å—Ç–≤—É—é—â–∏–π –ø–æ–¥–ø–æ–ª–∫–æ–≤–Ω–∏–∫ –º–∏–ª–∏—Ü–∏–∏ ‚Äî –æ –≤—ã–±–æ—Ä–∞—Ö –∏ –∏–∑–±–∏–µ–Ω–∏—è—Ö|url=https://news.tut.by/society/696994.html|access-date=18 August 2020|website=TUT.BY|language=ru}}</ref> 

In a 20 August statement by the [[United States Secretary of State]], Mike Pompeo underlined that the USA supported international efforts to look independently into Belarus‚Äô electoral irregularities, the human rights abuses that surrounded the election, and the crackdown that had followed.<ref name="Pompeo_20_August_statement"/>

In a 21 August statement by the [[Office of the United Nations High Commissioner for Human Rights|UN High Commissioner for Human Rights]], it was noted that, despite the majority of the detainees being released, serious concerns remained about the eight missing protesters and the sixty accused of serious criminal acts. The statement underlined the lack of information about the detainees' status and called for the government to stop unlawfully detaining people. The Commissioner also confirmed that there had been four deaths and was greatly concerned about the allegations of large-scale torture and ill-treatment of people, including journalists and children.<ref name="UNHC218">{{cite web |url=https://reliefweb.int/report/belarus/press-briefing-notes-belarus |title=Press briefing notes on Belarus |publisher=reliefweb |date=21 August 2020}}</ref> 

On 1 September, in a statement by the UN human rights experts, more than 450 documented cases of torture and ill-treatment of detainees were mentioned, including sexual abuse and rape with rubber batons of women and children.<ref name="UN_1_September_statement">{{cite web |url=https://www.ohchr.org/EN/NewsEvents/Pages/DisplayNews.aspx?NewsID=26199&LangID=E |title=UN human rights experts: Belarus must stop torturing protesters and prevent enforced disappearances |date=1 September 2020 |access-date=1 September 2020 |website=[[Office of the United Nations High Commissioner for Human Rights]]}}</ref>

The Ministry of Internal Affairs of Belarus rejected allegations of abuse and torture of citizens detained during the protests.<ref>{{Cite web|title=–í –ú–í–î –ë–µ–ª–∞—Ä—É—Å–∏ –æ—Ç—Ä–∏—Ü–∞—é—Ç –∏–∑–¥–µ–≤–∞—Ç–µ–ª—å—Å—Ç–≤–∞ –Ω–∞–¥ –∑–∞–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∞–Ω–Ω—ã–º–∏ –≤ –∫–∞–º–µ—Ä–∞—Ö|url=https://focus.ua/world/461120-v_mvd_belarusi_otritsaiut_izdevatelstva_nad_zaderzhannymi_v_kamerakh|access-date=22 August 2020|website=–§–û–ö–£–°|language=ru-UA}}</ref> However, the beatings of the detainees, including at Okrestina, were recognized by Alexander Lukashenko himself.<ref>{{Cite web|last=–í–ª–∞–¥—ã–∫–æ|first=–ê–ª–µ–∫—Å–∞–Ω–¥—Ä|date=17 August 2020|title=–õ—É–∫–∞—à–µ–Ω–∫–æ –ø—Ä–æ –¶–ò–ü –Ω–∞ –û–∫—Ä–µ—Å—Ç–∏–Ω–∞: –ø–æ–ª—É—á–∏–ª–∏ —Ç–µ, –∫—Ç–æ –±—Ä–æ—Å–∞–ª—Å—è –Ω–∞ –º–µ–Ω—Ç–æ–≤ - –õ—é–¥–∏ Onliner|url=https://people.onliner.by/2020/08/17/lukashenko-pro-okrestino-poluchili-te-kto-brosalsya-na-mentov|access-date=28 August 2020|website=Onliner|language=ru}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|date=22 August 2020|title="60% —Ñ–æ—Ç–æ - —Ñ–µ–π–∫–∏", "–≤—ã –∏—Ö –ø—Ä–æ—Å—Ç–∏—Ç–µ". –õ—É–∫–∞—à–µ–Ω–∫–æ –≤ –ì—Ä–æ–¥–Ω–æ –ø–æ—è—Å–Ω–∏–ª –¥–µ–π—Å—Ç–≤–∏—è –û–ú–û–ù–∞ –∏ —Ä–∞—Å—Å–∫–∞–∑–∞–ª –æ –≥–∏–±—Ä–∏–¥–Ω–æ–π –≤–æ–π–Ω–µ –ø—Ä–æ—Ç–∏–≤ –ë–µ–ª–∞—Ä—É—Å–∏|url=https://ru.hrodna.life/2020/08/22/lukashenko-omon/|access-date=28 August 2020|website=Hrodna.life - —Ä—É—Å—Å–∫–∞—è –≤–µ—Ä—Å–∏—è|language=ru-RU}}</ref>

On 26 October, Anais Marin the [[United Nations|UN]] human rights investigator, called on the Belarus government to "stop repressing its own people". About 20,000 people were detained in August and September, while hundreds have been reportedly beaten, intimidated, tortured or ill-treated in custody, according to the sources described by Anais Marin. [[Belarus]] has witnessed large-scale demonstrations against President [[Alexander Lukashenko|Alexander Lukashenko's]] re-election to a sixth term in the August 9 voting, which the opposition argues was rigged.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.stripes.com/news/europe/un-investigator-says-belarus-must-stop-repressing-its-people-1.650046|title=UN investigator says Belarus must stop repressing its people|accessdate=27 October 2020|website=Stars and Stripes}}</ref>

On 3 November 2020, [[United Nations|UN]] experts criticized Belarus government for targeting women human rights defenders, during the mass protests. Three women human rights defenders were detained & persecuted by the authorities for their work as rights activists in September and early October.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://news.un.org/en/story/2020/11/1076822|title=Belarus targets women human rights defenders after disputed August elections |accessdate=3 November 2020|website=UN News}}</ref>

On 6 November 2020, [[Organisation for Security and Co-operation in Europe]] revealed in a letter about the massive and systematic human rights violations and serious cases of torture in [[Belarus]], following the elections, where security forces used excessive violence against protesters. The report also stated to hold new Presidential elections and initiated an investigation into allegations of torture.<ref>{{cite web|url= https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/europe/belarus-elections-torture-human-rights-b1638750.html |title= Belarus should hold new elections after massive and systemic' human rights violations, report finds |accessdate= 6 November 2020 |website= The Independent }}</ref>

On 15 November 2020, the [[United Nations|UN]] human rights office said the government of Belarus continued to commit human rights violations with impunity against peaceful protesters three months after the country‚Äôs disputed presidential elections. The government had responded to these peaceful demonstrations in a heavy-handed manner, with the use of unnecessary or excessive force by law enforcement officials.<ref name=voa_11-15 />

On 22 November more then 200 people were detained in Minsk.<ref>{{cite web
 |language      = ru
 |url         =https://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/europe/belarus-protests-lukashenko-latest-b1759972.html
 |title       = Dozens arrested as thousands of demonstrators join Belarus protests
 |publisher   =Reuters
 |date        = 2020-11-22
 |accessdate  = 2020-11-24
}}</ref><ref>{{cite web
 |language      = ru
 |url         =https://tass.com/world/1226527
 |title       = Over 200 protesters detained in Minsk on Sunday - police
 |publisher   =TASS
 |date        = 2020-11-22
 |accessdate  = 2020-11-24
}}</ref>

==Attacks on journalists and censorship==
{{main|Censorship in Belarus}}

During the [[2020 Belarusian presidential election]], the cases of attacks increased. On 23 July Lukashenko during a meeting with the leaders of the country's economic bloc, his main concern was that the [[BBC]] and [[Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty]] had encouraged riots while streaming protests and threatened to expel media and ban them from reporting on the election.<ref>{{cite news|date=23 July 2020|title=Belarus: Leader Threatens to Expel Media Over Election News|work=The Washington Post|agency=Associated Press|url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/belarus-leader-threatens-to-expel-media-over-election-news/2020/07/23/8c2b073a-ccf3-11ea-99b0-8426e26d203b_story.html}}</ref>

On 9‚Äì11 August, several independent journalists were arrested in Minsk, Brest, and Babruysk.<ref name="t696210"/> According to a statement by the Belarusian Association of Journalists, on 10 August, internal troops and other government forces deliberately shot rubber bullets at independent journalists in Minsk (including [[Tut.by]] and [[Nasha Niva]]). The journalists wore special high visibility jackets and had personal IDs. Nasha Niva editor-in-chief (also wearing a jacket) disappeared during the night. He managed to send an [[SOS]] [[SMS]] message to his wife, saying he was arrested. His fate was unknown as of 13:30 local time, and the Nasha Niva website was not updated for many hours after his presumed arrest.<ref>[https://people.onliner.by/2020/08/11/zaderzhali-redaktora-nashej-nivy –û –∑–∞–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∞–Ω–Ω–æ–º —Ä–µ–¥–∞–∫—Ç–æ—Ä–µ "–ù–∞—à–µ–π –ù–∏–≤—ã"]. People.onliner.by (11 August 2020). Retrieved on 12 August 2020.</ref> Several journalists, including foreigners, were slightly injured during the suppression of the protests. A rubber bullet hit the plastic ID of Getty Images' photojournalist Michal Fridman. Several Russian journalists from both official media and Internet projects were arrested but soon released.<ref name="jour">[https://news.tut.by/society/696218.html –í –ú–∏–Ω—Å–∫–µ –ø—Ä–æ–ø–∞–ª–∏ —Ñ–æ—Ç–æ–∫–æ—Ä—Ä–µ—Å–ø–æ–Ω–¥–µ–Ω—Ç –ú–ò–ê ¬´–†–æ—Å—Å–∏—è —Å–µ–≥–æ–¥–Ω—è¬ª –∏ –≥–ª–∞–≤—Ä–µ–¥ ¬´–ù–∞—à–∞–π –ù—ñ–≤—ã¬ª. –ü–æ—Å—Ç—Ä–∞–¥–∞–ª–∏ –Ω–µ—Å–∫–æ–ª—å–∫–æ –∂—É—Ä–Ω–∞–ª–∏—Å—Ç–æ–≤]. News.tut.by (11 August 2020). Retrieved on 12 August 2020.</ref>

On 10 August, local journalists reported problems with all major communication platforms and pro-opposition websites.<ref name=":2"/>

On 11 August, it was reported that police officers and other government agents forcibly took away memory cards from many journalists' devices. They also forced them to delete photos or sometimes crushed their cameras.<ref name="t5"/> [[BBC News]] Russia reported that three of its journalists were beaten by the government forces that night while covering the protests.<ref>Kozenko, Andrei; Ivshina, Olga; Prosvirova, Olga and Zakharov, Andrei (9 August 2020) [https://www.bbc.com/russian/live/news-53698604 –ü—Ä–æ—Ç–µ—Å—Ç—ã –≤ –ë–µ–ª–∞—Ä—É—Å–∏: –ø–æ—Å–ª–µ —Ç—Ä–µ—Ç—å–µ–π –Ω–æ—á–∏ —Å—Ç–æ–ª–∫–Ω–æ–≤–µ–Ω–∏–π –∑–∞–ø—Ä–µ—Ç–∏–ª–∏ –ø–∏—Ä–æ—Ç–µ—Ö–Ω–∏–∫—É]. Bbc.com. Retrieved on 12 August 2020.</ref> Russian journalist Nikita Telizhenko was heavily beaten in Belarusian jail: he was arrested in Minsk and sent to [[Zhodzina]] because of jails' overcrowding in Minsk. In Zhodzina he was beaten on his kidneys, legs, and neck, but he was soon released at the Russian embassy's request.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.znak.com/2020-08-12/korrespondent_znak_com_nikita_telizhenko_byl_izbit_v_ivs_zhodinskogo_rayona_belorussii|title=–ö–æ—Ä—Ä–µ—Å–ø–æ–Ω–¥–µ–Ω—Ç Znak.com –ù–∏–∫–∏—Ç–∞ –¢–µ–ª–∏–∂–µ–Ω–∫–æ –±—ã–ª –∏–∑–±–∏—Ç –≤ –ò–í–° –ñ–æ–¥–∏–Ω—Å–∫–æ–≥–æ —Ä–∞–π–æ–Ω–∞ –ë–µ–ª–æ—Ä—É—Å—Å–∏–∏|website=www.znak.com}}</ref> Arrested Russian journalist Artyom Vazhenkov was reported to be accused of mass rioting (up to 15 years of prison in Belarus).<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.znak.com/2020-08-13/koordinatoru_otkrytoy_rossii_grozit_do_15_let_kolonii_v_belorussii|title=–ö–æ–æ—Ä–¥–∏–Ω–∞—Ç–æ—Ä—É "–û—Ç–∫—Ä—ã—Ç–æ–π –†–æ—Å—Å–∏–∏", –∑–∞–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∞–Ω–Ω–æ–º—É –≤ –ë–µ–ª–æ—Ä—É—Å—Å–∏–∏, –≥—Ä–æ–∑–∏—Ç –¥–æ 15 –ª–µ—Ç –∫–æ–ª–æ–Ω–∏–∏|website=www.znak.com}}</ref>

On 12 August, [[Belsat]] journalist Jauhien Merkis was arrested in Gomel while covering the protests. Even though he was there as a journalist, the next day, the local court sentenced him to 15 days in jail for "participation in an unauthorized mass event".<ref>[https://naviny.by/new/20200813/1597340087-v-gomele-arestovali-zhurnalista-evgeniya-merkisa –í –ì–æ–º–µ–ª–µ –∞—Ä–µ—Å—Ç–æ–≤–∞–ª–∏ –∂—É—Ä–Ω–∞–ª–∏—Å—Ç–∞ –ï–≤–≥–µ–Ω–∏—è –ú–µ—Ä–∫–∏—Å–∞]. Naviny.by (13 August 2020). Retrieved on 13 August 2020.</ref> He was liberated soon, but on 21 August he was arrested again and was given 5 days in jail.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://news.tut.by/society/697911.html|title=–ó–∞–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∞–Ω–Ω–æ–º—É –≤ –ø—è—Ç–Ω–∏—Ü—É –≤ –ì–æ–º–µ–ª–µ –∂—É—Ä–Ω–∞–ª–∏—Å—Ç—É-—Ñ—Ä–∏–ª–∞–Ω—Å–µ—Ä—É –¥–∞–ª–∏ 5 —Å—É—Ç–æ–∫|date=24 August 2020|website=TUT.BY}}</ref> Journalist Ruslan Kulevich from Grodno, arrested on 11 August, was freed on 14 August with fractures of both hands.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://nn.by/?c=ar&i=257105|title=–£ –∂—É—Ä–Ω–∞–ª—ñ—Å—Ç–∞ hrodna.life –†—É—Å–ª–∞–Ω–∞ –ö—É–ª–µ–≤—ñ—á–∞ –ø–µ—Ä–∞–ª–æ–º—ã –∞–±–µ–¥–∑–≤—é—Ö —Ä—É–∫|website=–ù–∞—à–∞ –ù—ñ–≤–∞}}</ref>

One of the few communication systems that managed to avoid censorship is the independent Belarusian-owned {{ill|NEXTA|ru|NEXTA}} [[Telegram (software)|Telegram]] channel based in [[Warsaw]]. The channel's subscribers rose from 100,000 on election night to over a million after a day.<ref>{{Cite news|last=Kuryshko|first=Diana|date=12 August 2020|title=How messenger app bypassed Belarus news blackout|language=en-GB|work=BBC News|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-53753412|access-date=13 August 2020}}</ref> The channel publishes user-generated videos, photos, and comments of the protests.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-europe-53753412 |title=Belarus election: How Nexta channel bypassed news blackout |work=BBC News |date=12 August 2020}}</ref> The founder of NEXTA himself is facing up to 15 years of prison after being indicted by the regime.<ref>{{cite web |title=Criminal case launched against NEXTA. He faces up to 15 years in prison |url=https://belsat.eu/en/news/criminal-case-launched-against-nexta-he-faces-up-to-15-years-in-prison/ |website=belsat.eu |language=en}}</ref> The use of Telegram software provided the protesters with communication channels to share information and coordinate protest action.<ref>{{cite news |work=[[The Washington Post]] |date=September 11, 2020 |title=There's more to Belarus's 'Telegram Revolution' than a cellphone app |url=https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2020/09/11/theres-more-belaruss-telegram-revolution-than-cellphone-app/ |quote=highlighting the use of the popular messaging app for sharing information.}}</ref> NEXTA Live's audience shot to over 2&nbsp;million. Its sister channel NEXTA has more than 700,000 followers. Belarus of the Brain's is now over 470,000. Officials opened a criminal probe into Stepan Putilo, founder of NEXTA, on charges of fomenting mass riots.<ref name=nap/> Igor Losik, who founded Belarus of the Brain, was arrested before the election, but the channel also continues to operate.<ref name=nap>{{cite news |url=https://apnews.com/823180da2b402f6a1dc9fbd76a6f476b |title='Telegram revolution': App helps drive Belarus protests |last=Litvinova |first=Daria |publisher=AP News |date=21 August 2020}}</ref>

On 15 August, a meeting was held with the head of the upper chamber of Parliament of Belarus [[Natalia Kochanova]] and press Secretary of the President of Belarus [[Natalia Eismont]]. The audience, the workers at the Belarusian TV and radio company in Minsk, asked why the station was not broadcasting the truth. The officials had been escorted to the building by riot police who took control of the building.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.kxan36news.com/riot-police-took-custody-of-the-minsk-television-center |title=Riot police took custody of the Minsk television centre |publisher=kxan36 |date=15 August 2020}}</ref> Thousands of protesters outside demanded the station show people the truth. It was also reported that some staff had resigned and one hundred were planning to strike on Monday.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-europe-53790741 |title=Belarus: Thousands protest outside state TV building |publisher=BBC |last= Tikhanovskaya |first=Svetlana |date=15 August 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|date=16 August 2020|title=Lukashenko says Putin has offered help as Belarus gears for 'March of Freedom'|publisher=France 24|url=https://www.france24.com/en/20200816-lukashenko-says-putin-offers-help-as-belarus-protesters-plan-march-of-freedom}}</ref>

It was reported that on 18 June, reporters from various countries, arriving in Minsk airport, were pulled out of passport control, interrogated and locked up before being refused entry and being told to buy a plane ticket to some other country, in an attempt to suppress the media.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://news.postimees.ee/7044063/minsk-border-guards-watched-journalists-like-they-were-prisoners |title=Minsk border guards watched journalists like they were prisoners |publisher=Postimees |date=21 August 2020}}</ref>

On 21 August 72 or 73 websites were blocked in Belarus, including several independent news portals (Radio Liberty/Free Europe in Belarus ''svaboda.org'', ''by.tribuna.com'' sport news, ''euroradio.fm'', ''belsat.eu'', ''gazetaby.com'', ''the-village.me/news'' and others), electoral sites of Tsepkalo and Babaryko, "Golos" and "Zubr" platforms, ''spring96.org'' human rights portal, and several VPN services.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://42.tut.by/697663|title=–í –ë–µ–ª–∞—Ä—É—Å–∏ –æ–≥—Ä–∞–Ω–∏—á–∏–ª–∏ –¥–æ—Å—Ç—É–ø –∫ –¥–µ—Å—è—Ç–∫–∞–º —Å–∞–π—Ç–æ–≤. –í–æ—Ç —Å–ø–∏—Å–æ–∫|date=22 August 2020|website=42.tut.by}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://tech.onliner.by/2020/08/22/v-belarusi-zablokirovan-ryad-sajtov|title=–í –ë–µ–ª–∞—Ä—É—Å–∏ –∑–∞–±–ª–æ–∫–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞–Ω —Ä—è–¥ —Å–∞–π—Ç–æ–≤. –í —Ç–æ–º —á–∏—Å–ª–µ –∏ –°–ú–ò ‚Äì –¢–µ—Ö–Ω–æ–ª–æ–≥–∏–∏ Onliner|first=–í–∏—Ç–∞–ª–∏–π|last=–û–ª–µ—Ö–Ω–æ–≤–∏—á|date=22 August 2020|website=Onliner}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://nn.by/?c=ar&i=257631&lang=ru|title=–°—Ä–µ–¥–∏ –∑–∞–±–ª–æ–∫–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö ‚Äî –º–µ–≥–∞–ø–æ–ø—É–ª—è—Ä–Ω—ã–π —Å–ø–æ—Ä—Ç–∏–≤–Ω—ã–π —Å–∞–π—Ç By.tribuna.com|website=–ù–∞—à–∞ –ù—ñ–≤–∞}}</ref>

As of 21 August, the Belarusian edition of [[Komsomolskaya Pravda]] newspaper failed to print three editions, and [[Narodnaja Volya (newspaper)|Narodnaja Volya]] failed to print a newspaper edition (both newspapers had a contract with the government-controlled printing house). The Belarusian Association of Journalists stated that the real cause was not technical troubles, but an attempt to block information about the protests and violations of human rights.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://belapan.by/archive/2020/08/22/ru_1056325/|title=–ë–µ–ª–∞–ü–ê–ù. –ë–ê–ñ —Ç—Ä–µ–±—É–µ—Ç –æ—Ç –≤–ª–∞—Å—Ç–µ–π –ø—Ä–µ–∫—Ä–∞—Ç–∏—Ç—å –±–ª–æ–∫–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∫—É —Å–∞–π—Ç–æ–≤ –°–ú–ò –∏ –¥–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ –Ω–∞ –ø—Ä–µ—Å—Å—É|website=belapan.by}}</ref> Two other independent newspapers (Belgazeta and Svobodnye Novosti) also were unable to print new editions in Belarus.<ref>[https://nn.by/?c=ar&i=257898&lang=ru –°–≤–µ–∂—É—é ¬´—Ç–æ–ª—Å—Ç—É—à–∫—É¬ª ¬´–ö–æ–º—Å–æ–º–æ–ª—å—Å–∫–∞—è –ø—Ä–∞–≤–¥–∞¬ª –≤—ã–Ω—É–∂–¥–µ–Ω–Ω–æ –ø–µ—á–∞—Ç–∞–ª–∞ –≤ –†–æ—Å—Å–∏–∏]</ref> New editions of Komsomolskaya Pravda and Narodnaja Volya were printed in Russia, but the state network of newsstands "Belsoyuzpechat'" denied to take them for sale. These newspapers also reported that the post service delayed the delivery by subscription.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://news.tut.by/society/698187.html|title=–ë–µ–ª–æ—Ä—É—Å—Å–∫–∞—è "–ö–æ–º—Å–æ–º–æ–ª–∫–∞" –∏ "–ù–∞—Ä–æ–¥–Ω–∞—è –≤–æ–ª—è" –Ω–∞—á–∞–ª–∏ –ø–µ—á–∞—Ç–∞—Ç—å—Å—è –≤ –†–æ—Å—Å–∏–∏. –ù–æ —Ç–µ–ø–µ—Ä—å –∏—Ö –Ω–µ –±–µ—Ä—É—Ç –≤ –∫–∏–æ—Å–∫–∏|date=26 August 2020|website=TUT.BY}}</ref>

On 27 August, around 20 journalists, from both local and international media, were detained on Freedom Square in Minsk.<ref>{{Cite web|date=27 August 2020|title=Around 20 journalists arrested for covering anti-government protests in Belarus|url=https://metro.co.uk/2020/08/27/around-20-journalists-arrested-covering-anti-government-protests-belarus-13188536/|access-date=28 August 2020|website=Metro|language=en}}</ref><ref name="auto9"/><ref name="auto10"/> The journalists were taken to the Kastrychnitski district police supposedly to check their identity and accreditation.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.svaboda.org/a/30805964.html|title=–ù–∞ –º–µ–Ω—Å–∫–∞–π –ø–ª–æ—à—á—ã –°–≤–∞–±–æ–¥—ã –º–∞—Å–∞–≤–∞ –∑–∞—Ç—Ä—ã–º–∞–ª—ñ –∂—É—Ä–Ω–∞–ª—ñ—Å—Ç–∞—û. –°—è—Ä–æ–¥ —ñ—Ö ‚Äî —Ñ–∞—Ç–æ–≥—Ä–∞—Ñ –†–∞–¥—ã—ë –°–≤–∞–±–æ–¥–∞|website=–†–∞–¥—ã—ë –°–≤–∞–±–æ–¥–∞}}</ref>

On 29 August, accreditation of several foreign journalists was revoked; they worked for [[Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty]], [[Associated Press]], [[Reuters]], [[Agence France-Presse|AFP]], [[BBC]], [[ARD (broadcaster)|ARD]], [[Radio France Internationale]], [[Deutsche Welle]] and [[Current Time TV]]. It was reported that some of them (including [[Paul Hansen (photographer)|Paul Hansen]]) were deported from Belarus.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://news.tut.by/society/698567.html|title=–†–∞–±–æ—Ç–∞—é—â–∏—Ö –≤ –ë–µ–ª–∞—Ä—É—Å–∏ –Ω–∞ –∏–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—Ä–∞–Ω–Ω—ã–µ –°–ú–ò –∂—É—Ä–Ω–∞–ª–∏—Å—Ç–æ–≤ –º–∞—Å—Å–æ–≤–æ –ª–∏—à–∞—é—Ç –∞–∫–∫—Ä–µ–¥–∏—Ç–∞—Ü–∏–∏|date=29 August 2020|website=TUT.BY}}</ref> Independent news web sites ''naviny.by'' and ''nn.by'' ([[Nasha Niva]] were blocked in Belarus.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://tech.onliner.by/2020/08/29/nasha-niva|title=–í –ë–µ–ª–∞—Ä—É—Å–∏ –∑–∞–±–ª–æ–∫–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞–ª–∏ "–ù–∞—à—É –ùi–≤—É" –∏ naviny.by, –∂—É—Ä–Ω–∞–ª–∏—Å—Ç–æ–≤ –∏–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—Ä–∞–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö –°–ú–ò –ª–∏—à–∞—é—Ç –∞–∫–∫—Ä–µ–¥–∏—Ç–∞—Ü–∏–∏ - –¢–µ—Ö–Ω–æ–ª–æ–≥–∏–∏ Onliner|first=–ï–≤–≥–µ–Ω–∏—è|last=–®—Ç–µ–π–Ω|date=29 August 2020|website=Onliner}}</ref>

On 1 September, 6 Belarusian journalists who covered the protest march of students in Minsk were detained. Initially they were taken to the police office to check the documents, but later they were charged with "participation in an unauthorized mass event" and coordination of the protests.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://officelife.media/news/19996-shest-zhurnalistov-sudyat-po-state-za-uchastie-v-aktsii/ |title=–®–µ—Å—Ç–µ—Ä—ã—Ö –∂—É—Ä–Ω–∞–ª–∏—Å—Ç–æ–≤ —Å—É–¥—è—Ç –ø–æ —Å—Ç–∞—Ç—å–µ –∑–∞ —É—á–∞—Å—Ç–∏–µ –≤ –∞–∫—Ü–∏–∏ |date=2 September 2020 |access-date=2 September 2020 |website=officelife.media |language=ru }}</ref><ref>{{cite news |url=https://news.tut.by/society/699046.html |title=–î–µ–ª–∞ –∂—É—Ä–Ω–∞–ª–∏—Å—Ç–æ–≤ —Å–Ω–æ–≤–∞ –æ—Ç–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª—è—é—Ç –Ω–∞ –¥–æ—Ä–∞–±–æ—Ç–∫—É –≤ –†–£–í–î |date=2 September 2020 |access-date=2 September 2020 |publisher=[[tut.by]] |language=ru }}</ref>

Starting 5 October, only state-approved and sponsored media are allowed to act as journalists in Belarus. This was achieved through the issue of journalist licenses, which was first announced on 2 October after Tut.by and several other resources were stripped of their journalist mandates. The licenses are strictly issued by the Belarusian government and forbid all medias from chronicling protests, demonstrations and other material deemed as "anti-governmental" by the state.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://zik.ua/ru/news/world/v_belarusi_lishili_akkreditacii_vseh_zhurnalistov_inostrannyh_smi_982549 |title=–í –ë–µ–ª–∞—Ä—É—Å–∏ –ª–∏—à–∏–ª–∏ –∞–∫–∫—Ä–µ–¥–∏—Ç–∞—Ü–∏–∏ –≤—Å–µ—Ö –∂—É—Ä–Ω–∞–ª–∏—Å—Ç–æ–≤ –∏–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—Ä–∞–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö –°–ú–ò |publisher=Zik Ukraine |date=2 October 2020 |language=ru}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|url=https://www.dw.com/en/belarus-cancels-all-accreditation-for-foreign-journalists/a-55130433 |title=Belarus cancels all accreditation for foreign journalists |publisher=Deutsche Welle |date=2 October 2020}}</ref>

Photographers working for the Russian state-owned agencies Komsomolskaya Pravda and TASS were detained on 12 October during the second seniors' march.<ref>{{cite news|url=https://news.tut.by/society/703685.html |title=–ì–∞–∑ –∏ —Å—Ç—ã—á–∫–∏ —Å —Å–∏–ª–æ–≤–∏–∫–∞–º–∏ –Ω–∞ –º–∞—Ä—à–µ –ø–µ–Ω—Å–∏–æ–Ω–µ—Ä–æ–≤. –ß—Ç–æ –ø—Ä–æ–∏—Å—Ö–æ–¥–∏—Ç –≤ –ë–µ–ª–∞—Ä—É—Å–∏ 12 –æ–∫—Ç—è–±—Ä—è |publisher=[[tut.by]] |date=12 October 2020 |access-date=13 October 2020 |language=ru}}</ref>

On 12 November, anarchist activist and journalist [[Mikola Dziadok]] was arrested in a safe house in [[Asipovichy District]].<ref>{{cite web|url=https://naviny.media/new/20201112/1605191992-mvd-soobshchilo-o-zaderzhanii-blogera-aktivista-anarhistskogo-dvizheniya|title=–ú–í–î —Å–æ–æ–±—â–∏–ª–æ –æ –∑–∞–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∞–Ω–∏–∏ –±–ª–æ–≥–µ—Ä–∞, –∞–∫—Ç–∏–≤–∏—Å—Ç–∞ –∞–Ω–∞—Ä—Ö–∏—Å—Ç—Å–∫–æ–≥–æ –¥–≤–∏–∂–µ–Ω–∏—è –ù–∏–∫–æ–ª–∞—è –î–µ–¥–∫–∞|publisher=Naviny|date=12 November 2020|access-date=23 November 2020|language=ru}}</ref> His Telegram channel was captured by the police.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://42.tut.by/707646|title=–ù–µ–∏–∑–≤–µ—Å—Ç–Ω—ã–µ –ø–æ–ª—É—á–∏–ª–∏ –¥–æ—Å—Ç—É–ø –∫ Telegram-–∫–∞–Ω–∞–ª—É –∞–Ω–∞—Ä—Ö–∏—Å—Ç–∞ –î–µ–¥–∫–∞. –°–∞–º –ù–∏–∫–æ–ª–∞–π –∑–∞–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∞–Ω|language=ru|publisher=TUT|date=12 November 2020|access-date=23 November 2020}}</ref> He was beaten during the arrest.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://belsat.eu/en/news/anarchist-dzyadok-detained-and-beaten-by-police/|title=Anarchist Dzyadok detained and beaten by police|date=13 November 2020|access-date=23 November 2020|first=Mikalai|last=Dzyadok|publisher=[[Belsat]]}}</ref> The "Anarchist Black Cross" claimed that he was tortured in order to give access to his computer data.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://abc-belarus.org/?p=13349|title=–ù–∏–∫–æ–ª–∞—è –î–µ–¥–∫–∞ –ø–æ—Å–ª–µ –∑–∞–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∞–Ω–∏—è –ø—ã—Ç–∞–ª–∏ –¥–ª—è –¥–∞—á–∏ –ø–æ–∫–∞–∑–∞–Ω–∏–π –∏ –¥–æ—Å—Ç—É–ø–∞ –∫ –∫–æ–º–ø—å—é—Ç–µ—Ä—É|publisher=Belarus Anarchist Black Cross|language=ru|date=13 November 2020|access-date=23 November 2020}}</ref>

On November 19, NEXTA founder Stepan Putilo and former chief-editor Roman Protasevich were added to the terrorism list by the Belarusian KGB. The list includes 726 persons, Putilo and Protasevich are the only Belarusian citizen in it.<ref>{{cite web
 |language      = ru
 |url         =https://meduza.io/en/news/2020/11/19/belarusian-kgb-adds-creators-of-opposition-telegram-channel-nexta-to-terrorism-list
 |title       = Belarusian KGB adds creators of opposition Telegram channel 'Nexta' to terrorism list
 |publisher   =Meduza
 |date        = 2020-11-19
 |accessdate  = 2020-11-24
}}</ref>

==International reactions==
{{main|International reactions to the 2020 Belarusian presidential election and protests}}

[[File:BelarusElections2020-InternationalReaction.svg|thumb|upright=1.9|International reactions to [[2020 Belarusian presidential election|Lukashenko's re-election]]
{{legend|#0000ffff|Belarus}}
{{legend|#4daf4aff|Congratulated Lukashenko}}
{{legend|#e41a1cff|Not recognised result }}{{Legend|#F98989|Expressed criticism over conflict escalation}}{{legend|#c0c0c0ff|No reaction}}]]

Countries and organisations have voiced their opinions with some accepting and some rejecting the election result. Many have commented about the protests with more condemning the violence. Some have done the following actions in relation with Belarus.

===Economic sanctions===
* On 14 August, [[European Union|EU]] High Representative for Foreign Affairs and Security Policy [[Josep Borrell]] announced that the EU would bring in sanctions against Belarusian officials responsible for "violence and falsification".<ref name="BBC148"/><ref name="Euro148">{{cite news |url=https://www.euronews.com/2020/08/14/eu-announces-sanctions-against-belarus-over-violence-on-protesters-and-electoral-falsifica |title=EU announces sanctions against Belarus over 'violence' on protesters and electoral 'falsification' |publisher=Euro News |date=14 August 2020}}</ref> [[Charles Michel]], [[President of the European Council]] went further on 19 August saying the EU would soon impose sanctions on a "substantial number" of individuals responsible for violence, repression, and election fraud.<ref name="CNBC198">{{cite news |url=https://www.cnbc.com/2020/08/19/belarus-eu-pushes-for-new-elections-says-no-external-intervention.html |title=EU to impose sanctions on Belarusian officials for election fraud, calls for a new vote |last=Meredith |first=Sam |publisher=CNBC |date=19 August 2020}}</ref> The European Commission announced it would divert ‚Ç¨53&nbsp;million earmarked for Belarus away from the government and towards civil society, victims of the state crackdown on protesters and the country's fight against the [[COVID-19 pandemic|coronavirus pandemic]].<ref name="Sky198">{{cite news |url=https://news.sky.com/story/eu-threatens-belarus-sanctions-as-it-rejects-election-result-12052472 |title=EU threatens Belarus sanctions as it rejects election result |publisher=Sky News|date=19 August 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite news|last=Reuters|date=19 August 2020|title=EU Executive to Reroute 53 Million Euros to Help Civil Society, Fight Against COVID in Belarus|language=en-US|work=The New York Times|url=https://www.nytimes.com/reuters/2020/08/19/world/europe/19reuters-belarus-election-vonderleyen.html|access-date=19 August 2020|issn=0362-4331}}</ref><ref name="euro198"/>

* On 18 August, the [[Lithuanian parliament]] agreed to impose economic sanctions.<ref>{{cite web |url=https://wvva.com/2020/08/18/lithuanian-lawmakers-vote-for-sanctions-against-belarus/ |title=Lithuanian lawmakers vote for sanctions against Belarus NEW |publisher=WVVA |date=18 August 2020}}</ref>

* On 19 August, the Prime Minister of Slovakia stated that the [[Government of Slovakia]] introduced sanctions against Belarus in the new legislative session.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://slovensko.hnonline.sk/2196943-bieloruska-kriza-matovic-chce-ekonomicke-sankcie-proti-pachatelom|title=Bielorusk√° kr√≠za: Matoviƒç chce ekonomick√© sankcie proti p√°chateƒæom|website=slovensko.hnonline.sk}}</ref>

* On 10 September, the EU sanctions on Belarus were delayed by a [[Cyprus‚ÄìTurkey maritime zones dispute|separate dispute]] between [[Cyprus]] and [[Turkey]],<ref>{{cite news |title=Cyprus says its issues with Turkey not linked to EU Belarus sanctions (Updated) |url=https://cyprus-mail.com/2020/09/10/cyprus-says-its-issues-with-turkey-not-linked-to-eu-belarus-sanctions-updated/ |work=[[Cyprus Mail]] |date=10 September 2020}}</ref> which has [[Turkish invasion of Cyprus|occupied the northern part of Cyprus]] since July 1974. [[Greece]] and Cyprus are pushing for a sanctions on Turkey in a dispute in the Eastern Mediterranean.<ref>{{cite news |title=Greece Presses EU to Draw Up 'Severe' Sanctions on Turkey |url=https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-09-10/eu-efforts-to-influence-belarus-held-up-by-turkey-dispute |work=Bloomberg |date=10 September 2020}}</ref>

* On 29 September, personal sanctions against 8 members of the regime, including Alexander and Viktor Lukashenko, were imposed by the UK and Canada. The sanctions included travel bans and [[asset freeze]]s.<ref name="UK_gov_sanctions">{{cite web |url=https://www.gov.uk/government/news/belarus-uk-sanctions-eight-members-of-regime-including-alexander-lukashenko |title=Belarus: UK sanctions 8 members of regime, including Alexander Lukashenko |date=29 September 2020 |access-date=29 September 2020 |website=[[Government of the United Kingdom]] }}</ref>

* On 2 October, the EU imposed sanctions on 40 Belarusian officials. Lukashenko was exempted from the sanctions as the EU aims to encourage Lukashenko to engage in talks with the opposition. Hours later, Belarus retaliated with sanctions against EU officials.<ref name="EU_Bel_sanctions">{{cite news |last=Tidey |first=Alice |url=https://www.euronews.com/2020/10/02/belarus-eu-agrees-sanctions-on-40-officials-but-not-lukashenko |title=Belarus: EU agrees sanctions on 40 officials but not Lukashenko |publisher=[[Euronews]] |date=2 October 2020 |accessdate=3 October 2020 }}</ref>

* On 6 November, the EU imposed sanctions on Belarusian President Alexander Lukashenko and 14 other officials for repression of the pro-democracy movement following August‚Äôs contested election. Their assets in EU member states were frozen and they are banned from entering EU territory.<ref>{{cite news |title=EU slaps sanctions on Belarus leader Lukashenko for crackdown |url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-54846049 |work=BBC News |date=2020-11-06|access-date=2020-11-07}}</ref>

* On 19 November, the EU announced an upcoming list of sanctions targeting the country's firms and entrepreneurs that finance Lukashenko. According to Borrell, up to date no positive signs were seen from the regime and the new measures will increase economic pressure on the self-proclaimed president.<ref>{{cite web
 |language      = ru
 |url         =https://www.dw.com/en/eu-to-slap-sanctions-on-belarus-firms-close-to-lukashenko/a-55665427
 |title       =EU to slap sanctions on Belarus firms close to Lukashenko 
 |publisher   =Deutsche Welle
 |date        = 2020-11-19
 |accessdate  = 2020-11-24
}}</ref><ref>{{cite web
 |language      = ru
|author=Harper, Jo
 |url         =https://www.dw.com/en/lukashenko-belarus-brace-for-economic-winter-of-discontent/a-55612753
 |title       = Lukashenko, Belarus brace for economic winter of discontent
 |publisher   =Deutsche Welle
 |date        = 2020-11-17
 |accessdate  = 2020-11-24
}}</ref>

===Allegations of foreign interference===
According to Russia's press service statement issued on 19 August 2020, "Russia pointed out that foreign attempts to interfere in the country‚Äôs domestic affairs were unacceptable and could further escalate tensions".<ref>{{Cite web|title=Putin tells Merkel foreign interference in Belarus' affairs is unacceptable|url=https://tass.com/politics/1190881|access-date=19 August 2020|website=TASS}}</ref> As Georgy Saralidze, advisor to the director of the [[All-Russia State Television and Radio Broadcasting Company]] on program policy, noted in an interview with Vestnik Kavkaza that western countries had been striving to isolate Belarus away from Russia for several years. "The main goal is to prevent the expansion of the [[Union State]], and ideally just to destroy it. What Vladimir Putin said to Merkel and Macron is a very symptomatic thing, because now there are attacks that Russia allegedly interferes in the affairs of Belarus. Moreover, there are no statements on the part of Russia, apart from the recognition of the election results. If you call it interference, then those who do not recognize the election also interfere in the affairs of Belarus."<ref>{{Cite web|title=–ú–æ—Å–∫–≤–∞ –ø—Ä–∏–∑–≤–∞–ª–∞ –ü–∞—Ä–∏–∂ –∏ –ë–µ—Ä–ª–∏–Ω –Ω–µ –≤–º–µ—à–∏–≤–∞—Ç—å—Å—è –≤ –¥–µ–ª–∞ –ë–µ–ª–∞—Ä—É—Å–∏|url=https://vestikavkaza.ru/news/makron-ekstrenno-pozvonil-putinu-po-belarusi.html|access-date=19 August 2020|website=vestikavkaza.ru|language=ru-RU}}</ref>

Lukashenko announced a week after the election that [[NATO]] forces were "at the gates" and threatening the country (which was denied by NATO<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.nato.int/cps/en/natohq/news_177525.htm |title=NATO Secretary General discusses Belarus with President of Poland |publisher=NATO |date=18 August 2020}}</ref>), prompting President Putin to offer to send in military assistance,<ref name="DW168"/> A Kremlin spokesman, [[Dmitry Peskov]], on 19 August said that there was no need for Russia to help Belarus militarily or otherwise at present.<ref name="BBC198"/> Belarus and Russia are members of the [[Collective Security Treaty Organisation]] (CSTO), a Russia-led military alliance of six former Soviet states,<ref>{{cite news |title=Is Belarus closer to the West or to Russia? |url=https://www.dw.com/en/belarus-european-union-russia/a-54613952 |work=Deutsche Welle |date=18 August 2020}}</ref> and part of a [[Union State of Russia and Belarus|Belarus‚ÄìRussia Union State]].<ref name="foreignmeddling">{{cite news |title=Russia Slams 'Foreign Meddling' in Belarus, Rules Out Immediate Military Aid |url=https://www.themoscowtimes.com/2020/08/19/russia-slams-foreign-meddling-in-belarus-rules-out-immediate-military-aid-a71199 |work=The Moscow Times |date=19 August 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Kremlin Says It Sees No Need to Help Belarus Militarily for Now |url=https://www.nytimes.com/reuters/2020/08/19/world/europe/19reuters-belarus-election-kremlin.html |work=The New York Times |date=19 August 2020}}</ref> [[President of the European Council]] [[Charles Michel]] spoke on 19 August about interference in Belarus, "It‚Äôs important for both the EU and Russia to support the democratic process in Belarus. We want to avoid external interference in Belarus." He added that he had read recent statements from Kremlin that it does not intend to interfere militarily.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://www.brusselstimes.com/news/belgium-all-news/127514/2-in-3-no-longer-motivated-to-follow-belgiums-coronavirus-measures/ |title=EU no longer recognises Lukashenko as president of Belarus |publisher=Brussels Times |date=19 August 2020}}</ref>

On 18 September 2020, Belarus Foreign Minister accused [[United Nations Human Rights Council]] of meddling in [[Belarus]] internal affairs over the UN Human Rights Council's resolution calling for the close monitoring of alleged rights violations in Belarus. The resolution came after the violent crackdown on protests of disputed presidential election.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.france24.com/en/20200919-belarus-accuses-un-human-rights-council-of-interfering-in-internal-affairs|title=Belarus accuses UN Human Rights Council of interfering in internal affairs|accessdate=19 September 2020|website=France 24}}</ref>

==Support for victims==
Unregistered candidate [[Valery Tsepkalo]] created a non-profit organization "Belarus of the future". The primary goal of the program is to support citizens of Belarus who have suffered from political repression. Tsepkalo was not the first who started supporting them. Before him, people were self-organizing the funds with the same concept to support victims of oppression in Belarus, paying for received fines they received during the protests.<ref>{{Cite web|title=–ë–µ–ª–∞—Ä—É—Å—å –±—É–¥—É—â–µ–≥–æ ‚Äì –ì–ª–∞–≤–Ω–∞—è|url=https://belarus-future.org/|access-date=14 August 2020|website=belarus-future.org}}</ref>

[[File:Protest in Torun against Poland's new abortion laws 9.11.2020.3.jpg|thumb|9 November 2020 protest in [[Toru≈Ñ]] against Poland's new [[Abortion in Poland|abortion laws]]: protesters supporting Belarus democratic rallies]]
Mikita Mikado, the CEO of [[PandaDoc]], which has Belarusian roots, offered to support authorities (police officers, army and security forces) that want to retire, but cannot because for financial reasons.<ref name=":7">{{Cite web|title="–ï—Å–ª–∏ –ø—Ä–æ–±–ª–µ–º–∞ –≤ –¥–µ–Ω—å–≥–∞—Ö". –ú–∏–∫–∏—Ç–∞ –ú–∏–∫–∞–¥–æ –ø–æ–º–æ–∂–µ—Ç —Å–∏–ª–æ–≤–∏–∫–∞–º –ø–µ—Ä–µ–π—Ç–∏ –Ω–∞ —Å—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—É –¥–æ–±—Ä–∞|url=https://dev.by/news/milicia-s-mikado|access-date=15 August 2020|website=dev.by|language=ru}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|last=Zvezda|first=Sergey|date=13 August 2020|title=–ì–ª–∞–≤–∞ PandaDoc –ø—Ä–µ–¥–ª–æ–∂–∏–ª —Ñ–∏–Ω–∞–Ω—Å–æ–≤—É—é –ø–æ–º–æ—â—å –±–µ–ª–æ—Ä—É—Å—Å–∫–∏–º —Å–∏–ª–æ–≤–∏–∫–∞–º, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–µ –Ω–µ –º–æ–≥—É—Ç —É–π—Ç–∏ —Å–æ —Å–ª—É–∂–±—ã —Ç–æ–ª—å–∫–æ –∏–∑-–∑–∞ –¥–µ–Ω–µ–≥ ‚Äî –û—Ñ–ª–∞–π–Ω –Ω–∞ vc.ru|url=https://vc.ru/offline/149848-glava-pandadoc-predlozhil-finansovuyu-pomoshch-belorusskim-silovikam-kotorye-ne-mogut-uyti-so-sluzhby-tolko-iz-za-deneg|access-date=15 August 2020|website=vc.ru}}</ref> The CEO is planning to resign based on the latest events. He had published a video and asked to contact him directly to get full support.<ref name=":7"/> 

Alexander Shneerson, the CEO of ISSoft, announced "The Belarusian society has invested a lot in the IT industry. We are part of the people of Belarus and we believe that the time has come for IT specialists to support those who suffered during the peaceful protests."<ref>{{Cite web|last=–ò–≤–∞–Ω–µ–π–∫–æ|first=–°—Ç–∞–Ω–∏—Å–ª–∞–≤|date=14 August 2020|title=–ö–æ–º–ø–∞–Ω–∏—è ISsoft –≤—ã–¥–µ–ª–∏—Ç $500 —Ç—ã—Å—è—á –Ω–∞ –ø–æ–º–æ—â—å –ø–æ—Å—Ç—Ä–∞–¥–∞–≤—à–∏–º –≤ –∞–∫—Ü–∏—è—Ö ‚Äì –¢–µ—Ö–Ω–æ–ª–æ–≥–∏–∏ Onliner|url=https://tech.onliner.by/2020/08/14/kompaniya-issoft-vydelit-500-tysyach-na-pomoshh-postradavshim-v-akciyax|access-date=15 August 2020|website=Onliner|language=ru}}</ref>

The Polish Prime Minister [[Mateusz Morawiecki]] announced on 14 August an ‚Ç¨11&nbsp;million fund to help protesters get visas and settle in Poland. Poland would provide support for Belarusian independent media and non-governmental organisations and scholarships would also be available to Belarusian students in Poland.<ref name="Euro148"/> Lithuania offered medical assistance to injured protesters.<ref name="Euro148"/>

On 19 August the EU promised ‚Ç¨2&nbsp;million to assist the victims of state violence and ‚Ç¨1&nbsp;million to support independent media as part of a ‚Ç¨53&nbsp;million package to support a peaceful transition.<ref name="euro198">{{cite news |url=https://www.euronews.com/2020/08/19/eu-leaders-to-discuss-next-steps-for-belarus |title=Threat of new crackdown on protesters as EU signals support for 'peaceful transition' in Belarus |publisher=Euro News |date=19 August 2020}}</ref>

Mikhail Orda, chairman of the [[Federation of Trade Unions of Belarus]], called for law officers to investigate every case of violence in a detailed and objective manner, adding that the trade unions were willing to provide legal assistance to all victims.<ref>{{cite news |url=https://eng.belta.by/society/view/belarus-trade-unions-call-to-investigate-all-cases-of-violence-132725-2020/ |title=Belarus' trade unions call to investigate all cases of violence |publisher=BELTA |date=20 August 2020}}</ref>

==Symbols==
{{undue weight section|date=October 2020}}
[[File:Minsk Protest 2020-08-16 160959.jpg|thumb|Protesters are waving the flags of the [[European Union]] and red-and-white flags (the official Belarusian flag from 1991 to 1995) during a rally against Lukashenko.]]
The [[Flag of Belarus#White-red-white flag|red-and-white flag]], the [[List of Belarusian flags|official flag of independent Belarus]] from 1991 to 1995, has been adopted by the pro-democracy opposition, becoming a powerful symbol. ''De facto'' banned by the authorities, the flag has been frequently confiscated by the police at demonstrations<ref name="auto8"/> and became a symbol for everyone who actively opposes Lukashenko.<ref name="auto2"/> Other symbols used by opposition supporters include the former [[National emblem of Belarus|coat of arms of Belarus]], known as the [[Pahonia]] (the historical coat of arms of the [[Grand Duchy of Lithuania]]),<ref>{{cite news |title=Split Identity and a Tug-of-War for Belarus's Memory |url=https://jamestown.org/program/84916/ |work=The Jamestown Foundation |date=20 December 2019}}</ref> and the song ''[[Vajacki mar≈°]]'',<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gLmwvUrEMQA |title=Video |website=www.youtube.com |accessdate=30 August 2020}}</ref> which was the national anthem of the short-lived [[Belarusian People's Republic]], as well as the song ''[[Pahonia (anthem)|Pahonia]]'' (lyrics based on the eponymous poem by [[Maksim Bahdanoviƒç|Maksim Bahdanovich]], music by Mikola Kulikovich).<ref>{{Cite web|title=Pesnyary - –ü–∞–≥–æ–Ω—è (Pagonya) lyrics + English translation|url=https://lyricstranslate.com/en/%D0%BF%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%8F-pahonia.html|access-date=2020-10-01|website=lyricstranslate.com|language=en}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=evoKG8LsjhU&t=132s |title=Video |website=www.youtube.com |accessdate=30 August 2020}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|title=–û—Å–æ–±–µ–Ω–Ω–æ—Å—Ç–∏ "–±–µ–ª–∞—Ä—É—Å–∫–∞–≥–∞ –∞–¥—Ä–∞–¥–∂—ç–Ω–Ω—è" –≤ 1918‚Äì1920‚Äì—Ö –≥–æ–¥–∞—Ö ‚Äî –í–æ–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–π –∏–Ω—Ñ–æ—Ä–º–∞—Ü–∏–æ–Ω–Ω—ã–π –ø–æ—Ä—Ç–∞–ª –ú–∏–Ω–∏—Å—Ç–µ—Ä—Å—Ç–≤–∞ –æ–±–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—ã –†–µ—Å–ø—É–±–ª–∏–∫–∏ –ë–µ–ª–∞—Ä—É—Å—å|url=https://www.mil.by/ru/news/press_center/publications/76519/|access-date=19 August 2020|website=www.mil.by}}</ref> A common slogan used by protesters is the phrase [[Long Live Belarus!]] (–ñ—ã–≤–µ –ë–µ–ª–∞—Ä—É—Å—å!, romanised: ''≈Ωyvie Bie≈Çaru≈õ!'').<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/world-europe-53762995|title=Shocked by violence, Belarusians lose their fear|first=Tatsiana|last=Melnichuk|date=13 August 2020|via=www.bbc.com}}</ref><ref>{{Cite web|url=https://www.euronews.com/2020/08/13/people-are-seeking-change-in-belarus-instead-they-re-being-mercilessly-beaten-and-detained|title=People are seeking change in Belarus. Instead, they're being mercilessly beaten and detained «Ä View|date=13 August 2020|website=euronews}}</ref> Anti-Lukashenko protesters have also used the current state flag of Belarus on rare occasions.<ref>{{Cite web|url=https://news.tut.by/society/697649.html|title=–ë–∞—Ä–∞–±–∞–Ω—ã, –≤—Å–µ —Ñ–ª–∞–≥–∏ –≤–º–µ—Å—Ç–µ –∏ "—Å–ª–æ–≤–æ –ø–∞—Ü–∞–Ω–∞". –í –í–∏—Ç–µ–±—Å–∫–µ –ø—Ä–∏–¥—É–º–∞–ª–∏ –Ω–æ–≤—ã–π —Ñ–æ—Ä–º–∞—Ç –º–∏—Ä–Ω—ã—Ö –∞–∫—Ü–∏–π|date=22 August 2020|website=TUT.BY}}</ref> In a few isolated cases anti-Lukashenko demonstrators have used the [[flag of Europe]].<ref>{{cite news |title=Belarus Protests Eclipse Rally in Defense of Defiant Leader |url=https://www.nytimes.com/2020/08/16/world/europe/belarus-protests-lukashenko.html |work=The New York Times |date=16 August 2020}}</ref>

The current state [[flag of Belarus]] has been universally used at demonstrations in support of Alexander Lukashenko.<ref>{{cite news |title=Belarus prosecutors open probe against opposition activists |url=https://www.belfasttelegraph.co.uk/news/world-news/belarus-prosecutors-open-probe-against-opposition-activists-39465469.html |work=Belfast Telegraph |date=20 August 2020}}</ref><ref name="AFP-flag"/> In a few isolated cases pro-Lukashenko demonstrators have used the [[flag of Russia]], the [[Banner of Victory]] against [[Nazi Germany]], the [[flag of the Soviet Union]] and the [[Ribbon of Saint George]].<ref>{{cite news |title=Rally in Minsk in support of Lukashenko |url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=UT4hmN-5Jeg |agency=Associated Press |date=21 August 2020}}</ref><ref name="AFP-flag">{{cite news |title=Belarus: 'Za Batku', pro-Lukashenko demonstrators gather in Minsk |url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=qNfPw4RvPNo |agency=Agence France-Presse |date=25 August 2020}}</ref><ref>{{cite news |title=Belarus: Thousands attend rally in support of Lukashenko in Vitebsk |url=https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=K30AK8dsfi8 |date=21 August 2020}}</ref>
